## 2026-06-10T06:33:50.833923+00:00 · 9d50cebd
- **Source**: claude_code
- **Category**: user
- **Session**: 2026-06-10
- **Prompt**:

  > Agentic AI Components
  > Component	Meaning	Purpose
  > Agent Catalog	List of all agents	Shows available agents: incident, security, deployment, Kubernetes, service explorer
  > Agent Registry	Official source of agents	Stores agent metadata, owner, version, status, permissions, tools
  > Agent Blueprint	Agent schema	Defines what every agent must contain
  > Agent Entity	Actual agent	Example: kubernetes-healing-agent
  > Agent Skill	Capability	Example: diagnose pod, restart pod, create Jira ticket
  > Skill Registry	List of approved skills	Controls reusable skills across agents
  > Agent Tool Mapping	Agent-to-tool permission	Defines which tools agent can use
  > Agent Action Mapping	Agent-to-action permission	Defines which Port actions agent can execute
  > Agent MCP Mapping	Agent-to-MCP access	Defines which external MCP servers/tools agent can use
  > Agent Flow	Execution sequence	Defines how agent thinks, selects tool, acts, audits
  > Agent Linking	Agent-to-agent relation	Allows one agent to call or depend on another agent
  > Agent Invocation	Runtime execution record	Stores every agent interaction for audit/debugging
  > Agent Scorecard	Quality score	Measures success rate, latency, safety, cost
  > Agent Governance	Control layer	RBAC, approval, audit, allowed autonomy
  > 
  > Port docs mention _ai_agent for agent configuration and _ai_invocations for execution/audit records. They also mention allowed tools, allowed actions, MCP connector access, permissions, and audit trail.
  > 
  > 1. Agent Catalog
  > Agent Catalog
  > │
  > ├── Incident Manager Agent
  > ├── Kubernetes Healing Agent
  > ├── Security Compliance Agent
  > ├── Deployment Orchestration Agent
  > ├── PR Enricher Agent
  > ├── Service Explorer Agent
  > ├── Platform Request Triage Agent
  > ├── Task Manager Agent
  > └── Vulnerability Remediation Agent
  > 2. Agent Registry
  > Field	Example
  > Agent ID	k8s-healing-agent
  > Agent Name	Kubernetes Healing Agent
  > Domain	Infrastructure
  > Owner	Platform Team
  > Version	v1.2
  > Status	Active
  > Autonomy Level	Approval Required / Automatic
  > Allowed Skills	Diagnose Pod, Restart Pod
  > Allowed Tools	Kubernetes, PagerDuty, Slack
  > Allowed MCP	GitHub MCP, Slack MCP
  > Runtime	Port AI
  > Audit Blueprint	_ai_invocation
  > 3. Skill Registry
  > Skill	Description	Reusable By
  > Diagnose Incident	Analyze alerts, logs, recent deploys	Incident Agent, SRE Agent
  > Restart Pod	Restart failed Kubernetes pod	K8s Agent
  > Scale Workload	Increase replicas/resources	K8s Agent
  > Create Jira Ticket	Create issue with context	Incident/Security Agent
  > Enrich PR	Add service context to pull request	PR Agent
  > Generate RCA	Summarize incident root cause	Incident Agent
  > Remediate Vulnerability	Suggest or trigger fix	Security Agent
  > 4. Agent to Skill Mapping
  > Agent	Skill	Execution Mode
  > Kubernetes Healing Agent	Diagnose Pod Failure	Automatic
  > Kubernetes Healing Agent	Restart Pod	Approval Required
  > Incident Agent	Generate Incident Update	Automatic
  > Incident Agent	Create PagerDuty Note	Approval Required
  > Security Agent	Analyze Vulnerability	Automatic
  > Security Agent	Create GitHub Issue	Approval Required
  > 5. Agent to Tool Mapping
  > Agent	Tool	Purpose
  > Incident Agent	Catalog Query	Find service owner
  > Incident Agent	Scorecard Query	Check service maturity
  > Incident Agent	Slack Tool	Send update
  > K8s Agent	Kubernetes Tool	Check pod health
  > Security Agent	GitHub Tool	Create remediation issue
  > Service Agent	Port Action Tool	Run self-service action
  > 6. Agent to MCP Mapping
  > Agent	MCP Server	Allowed Tools
  > Incident Agent	Slack MCP	Send message, search channel
  > Security Agent	GitHub MCP	Create issue, read repo
  > Task Agent	Jira MCP	Search ticket, update ticket
  > Knowledge Agent	Notion/Confluence MCP	Search docs
  > Deployment Agent	GitLab/GitHub MCP	Read pipeline, trigger workflow
  > 
  > Important: Port docs say MCP connector tools can be used by agents in interactive chat, but not in automated workflows where no connected user exists.
  > 
  > 7. Agent Flow
  > User / Event / API
  >       ↓
  > Agent Selection
  >       ↓
  > Load Agent Registry
  >       ↓
  > Load Skills
  >       ↓
  > Check RBAC
  >       ↓
  > Check Allowed Tools
  >       ↓
  > Check MCP Access
  >       ↓
  > Plan Task
  >       ↓
  > Execute Skill
  >       ↓
  > Run Tool / Action / MCP
  >       ↓
  > Validate Result
  >       ↓
  > Create _ai_invocation Audit
  >       ↓
  > Return Response / Trigger Workflow
  > 8. Agent Linking
  > Incident Manager Agent
  >       ↓
  > Service Explorer Agent
  >       ↓
  > Kubernetes Healing Agent
  >       ↓
  > Slack Notification Agent
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Parent Agent	Linked Agent	Why
  > Incident Agent	Service Explorer Agent	Find owner and dependencies
  > Incident Agent	K8s Healing Agent	Diagnose infra issue
  > Security Agent	PR Agent	Create remediation PR
  > Deployment Agent	Change Risk Agent	Check release risk
  > 9. Final Agentic Blueprint Set for Port
  > Blueprint	Purpose
  > _ai_agent	Agent definition
  > _ai_invocation	Agent execution/audit
  > ai_skill	Reusable skill
  > ai_tool	Tool definition
  > ai_agent_skill_mapping	Agent-skill relation
  > ai_agent_tool_mapping	Agent-tool relation
  > ai_agent_mcp_mapping	Agent-MCP relation
  > ai_agent_flow	Flow/workflow definition
  > ai_agent_scorecard	Quality and safety score
  > ai_agent_policy	Governance and approval rules
  > 
  > This is the real Agentic Port architecture:
  > 
  > Agent Registry
  >    ↓
  > Agent Catalog
  >    ↓
  > Skills Registry
  >    ↓
  > Tool Mapping
  >    ↓
  > MCP Mapping
  >    ↓
  > Agent Flow
  >    ↓
  > Agent Invocation
  >    ↓
  > Scorecard + Audit + GovernanceLevel 1 — Agent Runtime Flow
  > 
  > Imagine:
  > 
  > User:
  > "Investigate production outage"
  > 
  > The flow is:
  > 
  > User
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Port AI Agent
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Load Agent Definition
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Load Skills
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Load Tools
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Build Plan
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Execute Tools
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Validate Results
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Generate Response
  >   │
  >   ▼
  > Store Invocation
  > What is Actually Stored?
  > 
  > Port stores an Agent Definition.
  > 
  > Think:
  > 
  > Agent:
  >   Name: Incident Agent
  > 
  > Skills:
  >   - Incident Analysis
  >   - Root Cause Analysis
  >   - Notification
  > 
  > Tools:
  >   - Query Catalog
  >   - Slack MCP
  >   - Jira MCP
  > 
  > Actions:
  >   - Create Incident
  >   - Send Notification
  > 
  > This is basically a registry.
  > 
  > Step 1 — Agent Discovery
  > 
  > User asks:
  > 
  > Investigate Production Incident
  > 
  > Port first finds:
  > 
  > Which agent should handle this?
  > 
  > Agent Catalog
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  > Security Agent
  > Kubernetes Agent
  > Deployment Agent
  > 
  > System chooses:
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  > Step 2 — Load Agent Registry
  > 
  > Port loads:
  > 
  > Agent Name:
  >  Incident Agent
  > 
  > Allowed Skills:
  >  Incident Analysis
  >  RCA
  >  Notification
  > 
  > Allowed Tools:
  >  Query Catalog
  >  Slack MCP
  >  Jira MCP
  > 
  > Allowed Actions:
  >  Create Ticket
  >  Send Message
  > 
  > This becomes runtime context.
  > 
  > Step 3 — Skill Selection
  > 
  > This is where reasoning starts.
  > 
  > User asks:
  > 
  > Investigate outage
  > 
  > Agent evaluates:
  > 
  > Skill 1:
  > Analyze Incident
  > 
  > Skill 2:
  > Find Owner
  > 
  > Skill 3:
  > Notify Team
  > 
  > Planner generates:
  > 
  > Plan:
  >   1. Find affected service
  >   2. Find owner
  >   3. Check incidents
  >   4. Notify team
  > Step 4 — Tool Selection
  > 
  > Now agent asks:
  > 
  > Which tool can help me?
  > 
  > Tool Registry:
  > 
  > Catalog Query Tool
  > Slack MCP Tool
  > Jira MCP Tool
  > 
  > Agent chooses:
  > 
  > Catalog Query
  > 
  > because it needs service information.
  > 
  > Step 5 — Context Retrieval
  > 
  > Agent queries:
  > 
  > SELECT
  >  service,
  >  owner,
  >  environment
  > 
  > from Port Catalog.
  > 
  > Returns:
  > 
  > Payment Service
  > 
  > Owner:
  > Platform Team
  > 
  > Environment:
  > Production
  > Step 6 — Agent Memory
  > 
  > Agent now stores:
  > 
  > {
  >  "service":"payment",
  >  "owner":"platform",
  >  "env":"prod"
  > }
  > 
  > into working memory.
  > 
  > Think:
  > 
  > Conversation State
  > 
  > Without memory:
  > 
  > Agent forgets previous step
  > 
  > which causes:
  > 
  > Repeated work
  > Step 7 — Agent Calls MCP
  > 
  > Agent needs incidents.
  > 
  > Uses:
  > 
  > Jira MCP
  > 
  > Flow:
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  >       │
  >       ▼
  > Jira MCP
  >       │
  >       ▼
  > Jira
  > 
  > Agent asks:
  > 
  > Any open incidents?
  > 
  > Returns:
  > 
  > INC-123
  > Payment Service
  > Step 8 — Agent Decision
  > 
  > Now agent has:
  > 
  > Service
  > Owner
  > Incident
  > 
  > Reasoning:
  > 
  > Incident Exists
  > 
  > Severity High
  > 
  > Notify Owner
  > Step 9 — Action Selection
  > 
  > Port has Actions.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Send Slack Message
  > Create Jira Ticket
  > Create PagerDuty Incident
  > 
  > Agent decides:
  > 
  > Run Action:
  > Notify Team
  > Step 10 — Action Execution
  > Agent
  >    │
  >    ▼
  > Port Action
  >    │
  >    ▼
  > Slack
  > 
  > Message sent.
  > 
  > Step 11 — Validation
  > 
  > This is critical.
  > 
  > Agent asks:
  > 
  > Did action succeed?
  > 
  > Response:
  > 
  > HTTP 200
  > 
  > or
  > 
  > Failure
  > Step 12 — Invocation Record
  > 
  > Port creates:
  > 
  > _ai_invocation
  > 
  > record.
  > 
  > Stores:
  > 
  > {
  >  "agent":"incident",
  >  "tools":["jira","catalog"],
  >  "actions":["notify"],
  >  "result":"success",
  >  "duration":"12s"
  > }
  > 
  > This is the audit trail.
  > 
  > Multi-Agent Flow
  > 
  > Now imagine:
  > 
  > Investigate outage
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  > 
  > I need infrastructure info
  > 
  > calls:
  > 
  > Kubernetes Agent
  > 
  > Kubernetes Agent
  > 
  > I need metrics
  > 
  > calls:
  > 
  > Prometheus MCP
  > 
  > Returns:
  > 
  > CPU 98%
  > Memory 96%
  > 
  > Incident Agent continues.
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > Resource Exhaustion
  > Agent-to-Agent Runtime
  > Incident Agent
  >         │
  >         ▼
  > Service Explorer Agent
  >         │
  >         ▼
  > Kubernetes Agent
  >         │
  >         ▼
  > Security Agent
  > 
  > Each agent contributes specialized skills.
  > 
  > Real Enterprise Architecture
  > User
  >  │
  >  ▼
  > Planner Agent
  >  │
  >  ├─────► Service Agent
  >  │
  >  ├─────► Kubernetes Agent
  >  │
  >  ├─────► Security Agent
  >  │
  >  ├─────► Compliance Agent
  >  │
  >  └─────► Cost Agent
  > 
  > This is often called:
  > 
  > Agent Swarm
  > Agent Mesh
  > Agent Team
  > Multi-Agent System
  > What Architects Actually Design
  > 
  > You do NOT design prompts first.
  > 
  > You design:
  > 
  > Layer	What Architect Designs
  > Agent Catalog	Which agents exist
  > Skill Registry	What each agent can do
  > Tool Registry	Which tools are available
  > MCP Registry	Which MCP servers exist
  > Agent Mapping	Which agent can use which tool
  > Agent Flow	Orchestration
  > Memory Strategy	State management
  > Guardrails	Safety
  > Governance	RBAC
  > Evaluation	Agent quality
  > Audit	Invocation tracking
  > Cost Control	Token budget
  > Production-Grade Agent Runtime
  > Agent Registry
  >       ↓
  > Skill Registry
  >       ↓
  > Tool Registry
  >       ↓
  > MCP Registry
  >       ↓
  > Planner
  >       ↓
  > Memory
  >       ↓
  > Execution
  >       ↓
  > Validation
  >       ↓
  > Reflection
  >       ↓
  > Evaluation
  >       ↓
  > Audit
  >       ↓
  > Feedback LoopCustom App: AI Incident Automation Portal
  > 1. Department Use Case
  > 
  > Department: Insurance IT Operations
  > Use Case: AI Incident + Cloud Integration Automation
  > 
  > Goal:
  > 
  > Detect incident → analyze impact → find owner → check cloud/K8s/logs → recommend fix → create ticket → notify team → audit everything
  > 
  > Port AI Agents work with agent definitions, tools, actions, MCP connectors, permissions, and _ai_invocation audit records, so your custom app should copy the same pattern.
  > 
  > 2. Main UI Pages
  > UI Page	Purpose
  > Dashboard	Incident status, SLA, risk, agent activity
  > Incident Catalog	List of incidents
  > Service Catalog	Services, owners, environments
  > Agent Catalog	List of AI agents
  > Skill Registry	List of reusable skills
  > Tool Registry	APIs/MCP/cloud tools
  > Agent-Skill Mapping	Which agent can use which skill
  > Agent-Tool Mapping	Which agent can use which tool
  > Workflow Designer	Incident automation flow
  > Execution Trace	Step-by-step agent run
  > Audit Log	Who/what/when/action/result
  > Governance	RBAC, approval, guardrails
  > Reports	SLA, MTTR, failure trend, cost
  > 3. Database Tables
  > Core Catalog Tables
  > Table	Purpose
  > department	Insurance departments
  > team	Team ownership
  > user	Users
  > service_catalog	Apps/services
  > environment	Dev/QA/Prod
  > cloud_resource	AWS/Azure/GCP resources
  > incident	Incident records
  > runbook	SOP / fix guide
  > Agentic Tables
  > Table	Purpose
  > agent_registry	Master list of agents
  > skill_registry	Reusable skills
  > tool_registry	Tools/APIs/MCP
  > mcp_server_registry	MCP servers
  > agent_skill_mapping	Agent linked to skills
  > agent_tool_mapping	Agent linked to tools
  > agent_mcp_mapping	Agent linked to MCP servers
  > agent_flow	Workflow sequence
  > agent_invocation	Runtime execution/audit
  > agent_memory	Runtime state
  > agent_scorecard	Quality score
  > approval_request	Human approval tracking
  > 4. Example Agent Catalog
  > Agent	Purpose
  > Incident Triage Agent	Classify incident severity
  > Service Explorer Agent	Find service owner/dependency
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent	Check cloud/K8s health
  > RCA Agent	Generate root cause
  > Notification Agent	Send Slack/Email update
  > Ticket Agent	Create Jira/ServiceNow ticket
  > Governance Agent	Check approval/policy
  > 5. Skill Registry
  > Skill	Description
  > Classify Incident	Detect severity and category
  > Find Service Owner	Identify owning team
  > Analyze Logs	Read logs/errors
  > Check Cloud Health	Validate cloud resource status
  > Check Kubernetes Pods	Detect pod failures
  > Generate RCA	Summarize cause
  > Create Ticket	Open ServiceNow/Jira
  > Notify Team	Send Slack/Email
  > Recommend Fix	Suggest safe remediation
  > Request Approval	Ask human before risky action
  > 6. Agent-to-Skill Mapping
  > Agent	Skill
  > Incident Triage Agent	Classify Incident
  > Service Explorer Agent	Find Service Owner
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent	Check Cloud Health
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent	Check Kubernetes Pods
  > RCA Agent	Generate RCA
  > Ticket Agent	Create Ticket
  > Notification Agent	Notify Team
  > Governance Agent	Request Approval
  > 7. Tool / MCP Mapping
  > Tool/MCP	Connected System	Used By
  > ServiceNow MCP	Incident tickets	Ticket Agent
  > Slack MCP	Team notification	Notification Agent
  > Azure Monitor Tool	Cloud metrics	Cloud Diagnostic Agent
  > Kubernetes Tool	Pods/deployments	Cloud Diagnostic Agent
  > GitHub MCP	Recent deploys/PRs	RCA Agent
  > App Logs Tool	ELK/Datadog logs	RCA Agent
  > Email Tool	Escalation	Notification Agent
  > 
  > Port MCP connectors are used to connect external systems while keeping governance, RBAC, and audit controls centralized.
  > 
  > 8. End-to-End Process Flow
  > Incident Created
  >       ↓
  > Incident Triage Agent
  >       ↓
  > Service Explorer Agent
  >       ↓
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent
  >       ↓
  > RCA Agent
  >       ↓
  > Governance Agent
  >       ↓
  > Ticket Agent
  >       ↓
  > Notification Agent
  >       ↓
  > Audit + Scorecard
  > 9. Runtime Example
  > 
  > User or monitoring system creates:
  > 
  > Payment API is down in production
  > 
  > Flow:
  > 
  > Step	Action
  > 1	Incident Triage Agent classifies severity as P1
  > 2	Service Explorer Agent finds owner: Payments Team
  > 3	Cloud Diagnostic Agent checks Azure/K8s
  > 4	RCA Agent finds recent failed deployment
  > 5	Governance Agent checks if rollback needs approval
  > 6	Ticket Agent creates ServiceNow incident
  > 7	Notification Agent sends Slack update
  > 8	agent_invocation stores full audit
  > 10. Minimum Database Schema
  > CREATE TABLE agent_registry (
  >   agent_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >   agent_name VARCHAR(200),
  >   department_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   purpose TEXT,
  >   status VARCHAR(50),
  >   autonomy_level VARCHAR(50),
  >   owner_team VARCHAR(100)
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE skill_registry (
  >   skill_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >   skill_name VARCHAR(200),
  >   description TEXT,
  >   risk_level VARCHAR(50)
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE agent_skill_mapping (
  >   id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  >   agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   skill_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   execution_mode VARCHAR(50)
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE tool_registry (
  >   tool_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >   tool_name VARCHAR(200),
  >   tool_type VARCHAR(100),
  >   system_name VARCHAR(100),
  >   auth_type VARCHAR(100)
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE agent_tool_mapping (
  >   id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  >   agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   tool_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   permission_level VARCHAR(50)
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE incident (
  >   incident_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >   title TEXT,
  >   severity VARCHAR(20),
  >   service_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   status VARCHAR(50),
  >   created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > 
  > CREATE TABLE agent_invocation (
  >   invocation_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >   agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   incident_id VARCHAR(100),
  >   input_text TEXT,
  >   tools_used TEXT,
  >   action_taken TEXT,
  >   result TEXT,
  >   created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > 11. Tech Stack
  > Layer	Tool
  > Frontend	React / Next.js
  > Backend	FastAPI / Node.js
  > Database	PostgreSQL
  > Workflow	Temporal / LangGraph
  > Agent Layer	LangGraph
  > MCP	Custom MCP servers
  > Auth	OAuth2 / Keycloak
  > Observability	OpenTelemetry + Grafana
  > Logs	ELK / Datadog
  > Vector/RAG	Qdrant / Azure AI Search
  > LLM	Azure OpenAI / Claude / Gemini
  > 12. MVP Build Order
  > Phase	Build
  > Phase 1	Service catalog + incident catalog
  > Phase 2	Agent registry + skill registry
  > Phase 3	Agent-skill-tool mapping
  > Phase 4	Manual workflow execution
  > Phase 5	Add LangGraph agent flow
  > Phase 6	Add MCP connectors
  > Phase 7	Add approval + audit
  > Phase 8	Add dashboard + scorecards
  > Final Simple Architecture
  > React UI
  >   ↓
  > API Gateway
  >   ↓
  > FastAPI Backend
  >   ↓
  > PostgreSQL Catalog
  >   ↓
  > Agent Registry + Skill Registry
  >   ↓
  > LangGraph Orchestrator
  >   ↓
  > MCP Tools / Cloud Tools
  >   ↓
  > ServiceNow / Slack / Azure / GitHub
  >   ↓
  > Audit + Scorecard + DashboardBelow is the Agentic Tables design for your custom app. This copies the same idea as Port: agent definition, tools/actions, MCP access, invocation audit, governance, and monitoring. Port also uses _ai_agent and _ai_invocation concepts for agent configuration and audit tracking.
  > 
  > 1. agent_registry
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Master list of all agents
  > Example	Incident Agent, RCA Agent, Cloud Agent, Security Agent
  > Key Fields	agent_id, name, type, department, owner, status, version, autonomy_level, risk_level
  > How it works	Defines who the agent is, what domain it owns, and whether it is active
  > State	Draft, Active, Suspended, Deprecated
  > Integration	LangGraph, Port-like UI, workflow engine, RBAC
  > Issues	Wrong owner, duplicate agent, inactive agent used, outdated version
  > Solution	Versioning, approval before activation, owner validation, lifecycle policy
  > Monitoring	Agent health, success rate, failure rate, latency, cost
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Checks whether correct agent was selected
  > 
  > Sample fields
  > 
  > Column	Type	Example
  > agent_id	string	incident_agent
  > agent_name	string	Incident Triage Agent
  > agent_type	string	Planner / Worker / Supervisor
  > department	string	Insurance IT Ops
  > owner_team	string	Platform Team
  > status	string	Active
  > autonomy_level	string	Approval Required
  > version	string	v1.0
  > created_at	datetime	timestamp
  > 2. skill_registry
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Reusable capability library
  > Example	classify incident, generate RCA, check logs, notify team
  > Key Fields	skill_id, name, category, risk_level, input_schema, output_schema
  > How it works	Agents pick skills based on task intent
  > State	Draft, Approved, Retired
  > Integration	Agent registry, workflow engine, prompt templates
  > Issues	Skill too broad, unsafe skill, duplicate skill
  > Solution	Skill approval, input/output contract, risk classification
  > Monitoring	Skill usage count, success rate, error rate
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Validates whether selected skill matches task
  > 
  > Example skills
  > 
  > Skill	Category	Risk
  > Classify Incident	Analysis	Low
  > Find Service Owner	Catalog	Low
  > Restart Pod	Remediation	High
  > Create Ticket	Action	Medium
  > Generate RCA	Reasoning	Medium
  > Notify Team	Communication	Low
  > 3. tool_registry
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	List of tools/APIs available to agents
  > Example	Azure Monitor, Kubernetes API, Jira API, Slack API
  > Key Fields	tool_id, tool_name, tool_type, endpoint, auth_type, timeout, rate_limit
  > How it works	Agent uses tools to fetch data or perform action
  > State	Available, Down, Restricted, Deprecated
  > Integration	APIs, MCP, cloud, observability, ticketing
  > Issues	Tool timeout, wrong API permission, rate limit, bad response
  > Solution	Retry, circuit breaker, fallback tool, schema validation
  > Monitoring	Tool latency, timeout rate, error rate, usage count
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Blocks unsafe tool calls
  > 
  > Example tools
  > 
  > Tool	Type	System
  > Catalog Query Tool	Read	PostgreSQL
  > Azure Monitor Tool	Read	Azure
  > Kubernetes Tool	Action	AKS/EKS
  > Jira Tool	Action	Jira
  > Slack Tool	Action	Slack
  > Log Search Tool	Read	ELK/Datadog
  > 4. mcp_server_registry
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Registry of external MCP servers
  > Example	GitHub MCP, Slack MCP, Jira MCP, ServiceNow MCP
  > Key Fields	mcp_id, name, url, auth_type, owner, allowed_tools, status
  > How it works	Agent connects to approved MCP servers through controlled access
  > State	Connected, Disconnected, Auth Failed, Disabled
  > Integration	Claude, Cursor, Port MCP, custom MCP gateway
  > Issues	Auth failure, server down, unsafe write tools, user not connected
  > Solution	OAuth validation, read-only mode, allowed-tool filtering
  > Monitoring	MCP uptime, auth errors, tool usage, failed calls
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Ensures MCP tool is allowed before execution
  > 
  > Important limitation: Port docs mention MCP connector tools are mainly for interactive chat with connected user authentication, not fully automated contexts without a connected user.
  > 
  > 5. agent_skill_mapping
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Links agents to allowed skills
  > Example	Incident Agent → Classify Incident
  > Key Fields	mapping_id, agent_id, skill_id, execution_mode, priority
  > How it works	Agent can only use mapped skills
  > State	Active, Disabled
  > Integration	Agent registry, skill registry
  > Issues	Agent missing required skill, agent has risky skill
  > Solution	Approval workflow, skill risk review
  > Monitoring	Skill selection accuracy, failed skill execution
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Checks if skill is permitted
  > 
  > Example
  > 
  > Agent	Skill	Mode
  > Incident Agent	Classify Incident	Automatic
  > Incident Agent	Generate RCA	Approval Required
  > Cloud Agent	Check Kubernetes Pods	Automatic
  > Cloud Agent	Restart Pod	Approval Required
  > 6. agent_tool_mapping
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Links agents to allowed tools
  > Example	Cloud Agent → Kubernetes Tool
  > Key Fields	agent_id, tool_id, permission_level, execution_mode
  > How it works	Controls which tool each agent can call
  > State	Active, Disabled, Expired
  > Integration	Tool registry, RBAC, policy engine
  > Issues	Excessive permissions, wrong tool access
  > Solution	Least privilege, read-only default, approval for write tools
  > Monitoring	Tool calls by agent, blocked calls, failed calls
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Prevents unauthorized tool use
  > 7. agent_mcp_mapping
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Links agents to MCP servers
  > Example	Security Agent → GitHub MCP
  > Key Fields	agent_id, mcp_id, allowed_mcp_tools, auth_mode
  > How it works	Agent can only use selected MCP tools
  > State	Active, User Auth Required, Disabled
  > Integration	MCP gateway, OAuth, external systems
  > Issues	User not authenticated, write tool risk, expired token
  > Solution	Token refresh, read-only mode, action allowlist
  > Monitoring	MCP invocation logs, auth failures
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Verifies MCP access before tool call
  > 8. agent_flow
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Defines workflow sequence
  > Example	Incident → Triage → RCA → Approval → Notify
  > Key Fields	flow_id, name, trigger_type, steps, condition, fallback
  > How it works	Orchestrates multiple agents and tools
  > State	Draft, Active, Failed, Paused
  > Integration	LangGraph, Temporal, Airflow, n8n
  > Issues	Infinite loop, wrong routing, failed step
  > Solution	max steps, timeout, retry policy, fallback route
  > Monitoring	Step latency, failed node, loop count
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Watches the flow and stops unsafe execution
  > 
  > Example flow
  > 
  > Incident Created
  >   ↓
  > Incident Triage Agent
  >   ↓
  > Service Explorer Agent
  >   ↓
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent
  >   ↓
  > RCA Agent
  >   ↓
  > Approval Request
  >   ↓
  > Ticket Agent
  >   ↓
  > Notification Agent
  >   ↓
  > Audit
  > 9. agent_invocation
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Runtime execution and audit
  > Example	Agent run for incident INC-1001
  > Key Fields	invocation_id, agent_id, input, output, tools_used, status, duration
  > How it works	Every agent run creates a trace record
  > State	Running, Success, Failed, Cancelled
  > Integration	Audit, observability, Langfuse, OpenTelemetry
  > Issues	Missing trace, partial execution, unclear failure
  > Solution	correlation_id, trace_id, step logs
  > Monitoring	Success rate, latency, error category, token cost
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Reviews failed invocation and suggests fix
  > 
  > This is similar to Port’s _ai_invocation audit model.
  > 
  > 10. agent_memory
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Runtime state and memory
  > Example	Current incident, service owner, previous tool result
  > Key Fields	memory_id, session_id, agent_id, key, value, ttl
  > How it works	Stores temporary or long-term context
  > State	Active, Expired, Archived
  > Integration	Redis, PostgreSQL, Vector DB
  > Issues	Memory bloat, stale memory, wrong context
  > Solution	TTL, memory summarization, memory cleanup
  > Monitoring	Memory size, stale records, retrieval accuracy
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Detects stale or conflicting memory
  > 
  > Memory types
  > 
  > Type	Example
  > Session Memory	Current chat
  > Working Memory	Current incident
  > Long-Term Memory	Known service patterns
  > Vector Memory	Past RCA examples
  > 11. agent_scorecard
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Quality and safety score
  > Example	Incident Agent score = 87/100
  > Key Fields	scorecard_id, agent_id, metric, score, threshold
  > How it works	Measures agent production readiness
  > State	Pass, Warning, Fail
  > Integration	Dashboard, governance, release gate
  > Issues	Fake high score, missing metric, outdated threshold
  > Solution	automated evaluation, human review, baseline comparison
  > Monitoring	Trend, degradation, score drop
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Blocks poor-performing agent from production
  > 
  > Scorecard metrics
  > 
  > Metric	Target
  > Success Rate	>95%
  > Hallucination Rate	<5%
  > Tool Error Rate	<2%
  > Latency	<5 sec
  > Cost per Run	Within budget
  > Human Override Rate	<10%
  > 12. approval_request
  > Area	Details
  > Purpose	Human approval before risky action
  > Example	Restart production pod, rollback deployment
  > Key Fields	approval_id, agent_id, action, risk_level, approver, status
  > How it works	Agent pauses until human approves
  > State	Pending, Approved, Rejected, Expired
  > Integration	Slack, Teams, Jira, ServiceNow, Email
  > Issues	Approval delay, wrong approver, bypass risk
  > Solution	escalation, policy engine, approval SLA
  > Monitoring	approval time, rejection rate, expired approvals
  > Supervisor Agent Role	Ensures risky actions do not run automatically
  > Full Agentic Database Relationship
  > agent_registry
  >    ↓
  > agent_skill_mapping → skill_registry
  >    ↓
  > agent_tool_mapping → tool_registry
  >    ↓
  > agent_mcp_mapping → mcp_server_registry
  >    ↓
  > agent_flow
  >    ↓
  > agent_invocation
  >    ↓
  > agent_memory
  >    ↓
  > agent_scorecard
  >    ↓
  > approval_request
  > End-to-End Runtime Sequence
  > 1. Incident created
  > 2. Select correct agent
  > 3. Load agent_registry
  > 4. Load mapped skills
  > 5. Load mapped tools
  > 6. Load mapped MCP servers
  > 7. Start agent_flow
  > 8. Store runtime state in agent_memory
  > 9. Execute tool/action
  > 10. Request approval if high risk
  > 11. Store result in agent_invocation
  > 12. Update agent_scorecard
  > 13. Send notification
  > 14. Supervisor agent validates output
  > 15. Close or escalate incident
  > Common Issues and Mitigation
  > Issue	Where It Happens	Mitigation
  > Wrong agent selected	agent_registry	Better routing rules, classifier
  > Agent uses wrong skill	agent_skill_mapping	Skill validation, supervisor check
  > Tool timeout	tool_registry	Retry, fallback, circuit breaker
  > MCP auth failure	mcp_server_registry	Token refresh, OAuth validation
  > Infinite loop	agent_flow	max iteration limit
  > Memory stale	agent_memory	TTL, cleanup, summarization
  > Unsafe action	approval_request	Human approval
  > Poor answer	agent_scorecard	Evaluation and retraining
  > Missing audit	agent_invocation	Mandatory trace ID
  > High cost	invocation + scorecard	budget limit, model routing
  > Build To-Do List
  > Phase	Task
  > 1	Create database tables
  > 2	Build Agent Catalog UI
  > 3	Build Skill Registry UI
  > 4	Build Tool/MCP Registry UI
  > 5	Build mapping screens
  > 6	Build simple flow designer
  > 7	Add LangGraph orchestration
  > 8	Add approval workflow
  > 9	Add invocation audit page
  > 10	Add scorecard dashboard
  > 11	Add supervisor agent
  > 12	Add monitoring/tracing
  > UI Menu Structure
  > Menu	Screens
  > Dashboard	Agent health, incidents, scorecards
  > Catalog	Agents, Skills, Tools, MCP
  > Mapping	Agent-Skill, Agent-Tool, Agent-MCP
  > Workflow	Flow Designer, Flow Runs
  > Runtime	Invocations, Memory, Trace
  > Governance	Approvals, Policies, RBAC
  > Monitoring	Metrics, Logs, Cost, Errors
  > Flowchart
  > Incident/Event/User Request
  >         ↓
  > Agent Router
  >         ↓
  > Agent Registry Lookup
  >         ↓
  > Skill + Tool + MCP Mapping
  >         ↓
  > Policy Check
  >         ↓
  > Agent Flow Execution
  >         ↓
  > Tool / MCP / Action Call
  >         ↓
  > Result Validation
  >         ↓
  > Approval if High Risk
  >         ↓
  > Invocation Audit
  >         ↓
  > Scorecard Update
  >         ↓
  > Supervisor Agent Review
  >         ↓
  > Close / Escalate
  > Supervisor Agent Design
  > Supervisor Task	Purpose
  > Validate agent selection	Avoid wrong agent
  > Validate skill selection	Avoid wrong capability
  > Check tool permission	Stop unauthorized calls
  > Detect loops	Stop repeated execution
  > Review output quality	Reduce hallucination
  > Check policy	Enforce governance
  > Escalate to human	Handle uncertainty
  > Update scorecard	Continuous improvement
  > Best Architecture Approach
  > 
  > Start small.
  > 
  > Build only this first:
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  > Service Explorer Agent
  > Cloud Diagnostic Agent
  > RCA Agent
  > Notification Agent
  > 
  > Then add:
  > 
  > Skill Registry
  > Tool Mapping
  > Invocation Audit
  > Approval Request
  > Scorecard
  > Supervisor Agent
  > 
  > That will give you a complete working Agentic AI Department Automation App.Good. We start with Table 1: agent_registry.
  > 
  > 1. agent_registry — Master Agent Table
  > 
  > This is the main table where every AI agent is registered before it can be used.
  > 
  > Port has a similar idea using _ai_agent for agent configuration and _ai_invocation for execution/audit tracking.
  > 
  > Purpose
  > Item	Explanation
  > Main purpose	Store all agents in one place
  > Business use	Know which agents exist for a department
  > Technical use	Runtime loads agent configuration from this table
  > Governance use	Control status, owner, risk, approval, version
  > Example	Incident Agent, RCA Agent, Cloud Agent, Security Agent
  > Example Agents for Insurance IT Operations
  > Agent ID	Agent Name	Purpose
  > incident_triage_agent	Incident Triage Agent	Classifies incident severity
  > service_explorer_agent	Service Explorer Agent	Finds service owner and dependencies
  > cloud_diagnostic_agent	Cloud Diagnostic Agent	Checks Azure/Kubernetes health
  > rca_agent	RCA Agent	Generates root cause analysis
  > notification_agent	Notification Agent	Sends Slack/email updates
  > supervisor_agent	Supervisor Agent	Reviews agent decisions
  > Table Columns
  > Column	Type	Why Needed	Example
  > agent_id	string	Unique ID	incident_triage_agent
  > agent_name	string	Display name	Incident Triage Agent
  > agent_type	string	Agent role	Planner / Worker / Supervisor
  > department_id	string	Department owner	Insurance IT Ops
  > business_domain	string	Business area	Claims / Billing / IT Ops
  > purpose	text	What agent does	Classify incidents
  > owner_team	string	Responsible team	Platform Team
  > status	string	Lifecycle state	Draft / Active / Disabled
  > version	string	Change tracking	v1.0
  > autonomy_level	string	How much freedom	Manual / Approval / Auto
  > risk_level	string	Risk category	Low / Medium / High
  > model_name	string	LLM used	GPT-4o / Claude / Llama
  > runtime_framework	string	Agent engine	LangGraph / CrewAI
  > max_steps	number	Stop infinite loop	10
  > timeout_seconds	number	Execution limit	60
  > cost_limit	number	Budget control	2 dollars/run
  > created_by	string	Creator	architect user
  > created_at	datetime	Created time	timestamp
  > updated_at	datetime	Updated time	timestamp
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE agent_registry (
  >     agent_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >     agent_name VARCHAR(200) NOT NULL,
  >     agent_type VARCHAR(50),
  >     department_id VARCHAR(100),
  >     business_domain VARCHAR(100),
  >     purpose TEXT,
  >     owner_team VARCHAR(100),
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  >     version VARCHAR(50),
  >     autonomy_level VARCHAR(50),
  >     risk_level VARCHAR(50),
  >     model_name VARCHAR(100),
  >     runtime_framework VARCHAR(100),
  >     max_steps INT DEFAULT 10,
  >     timeout_seconds INT DEFAULT 60,
  >     cost_limit DECIMAL(10,2),
  >     created_by VARCHAR(100),
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
  >     updated_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > How It Works
  > User / Event
  >    ↓
  > Agent Router
  >    ↓
  > Search agent_registry
  >    ↓
  > Check status = Active
  >    ↓
  > Check department/domain
  >    ↓
  > Load agent config
  >    ↓
  > Load skills/tools/mcp mapping
  >    ↓
  > Start agent flow
  > Runtime Example
  > 
  > Incident comes in:
  > 
  > Payment API is down in production
  > 
  > System checks agent_registry:
  > 
  > Check	Result
  > Which domain?	IT Ops
  > Which agent?	Incident Triage Agent
  > Is agent active?	Yes
  > Risk level?	Medium
  > Autonomy?	Approval Required
  > Max steps?	10
  > Runtime?	LangGraph
  > 
  > Then it starts the agent.
  > 
  > Features
  > Feature	Description
  > Agent lifecycle	Draft, Active, Disabled, Retired
  > Ownership	Every agent has a business/technical owner
  > Versioning	Track v1, v2, v3
  > Autonomy control	Manual, approval-required, fully automatic
  > Risk control	Low, medium, high
  > Runtime control	LangGraph, CrewAI, custom
  > Cost control	Limit cost per run
  > Loop control	Max steps prevents infinite execution
  > Timeout control	Stop stuck agents
  > Limitations
  > Limitation	Why It Happens
  > Registry alone does not run agent	It only stores metadata
  > Skills are not stored here	Skills need skill_registry
  > Tools are not stored here	Tools need tool_registry
  > MCP access is not stored here	MCP needs agent_mcp_mapping
  > Runtime memory is not stored here	Memory needs agent_memory
  > Audit is not stored here	Audit needs agent_invocation
  > Issues That May Occur
  > Issue	Example	Solution
  > Wrong agent selected	Billing Agent handles cloud incident	Better routing rules
  > Duplicate agents	Two RCA agents	Naming/version policy
  > Inactive agent used	Disabled agent triggered	Status check before run
  > High-risk agent runs automatically	Restart pod without approval	Enforce autonomy level
  > Infinite loop	Agent keeps retrying	max_steps limit
  > Long execution	Agent stuck on tool call	timeout setting
  > Cost explosion	Too many LLM calls	cost limit
  > No owner	Agent has no accountable team	owner required field
  > Mitigation Strategy
  > Risk	Mitigation
  > Wrong agent	Agent router + supervisor validation
  > Unsafe automation	Human approval for high-risk agents
  > Agent drift	Versioning + scorecards
  > Poor performance	Monitor success rate and failure rate
  > Tool misuse	Tool mapping and RBAC
  > Audit gap	Mandatory invocation logging
  > Monitoring Metrics
  > Metric	Why It Matters
  > Agent usage count	Which agents are used most
  > Success rate	Is agent reliable?
  > Failure rate	Is agent broken?
  > Average latency	Is it slow?
  > Average cost	Is it expensive?
  > Human override rate	Is agent making poor decisions?
  > Timeout count	Is agent stuck?
  > Loop count	Is agent repeating steps?
  > Supervisor Agent Role
  > 
  > Supervisor agent checks:
  > 
  > Check	Purpose
  > Is this the right agent?	Prevent wrong routing
  > Is agent active?	Prevent retired agent execution
  > Is risk level acceptable?	Stop unsafe operation
  > Does it need approval?	Enforce governance
  > Is output valid?	Reduce hallucination
  > Did it exceed steps?	Stop infinite loop
  > Create / Delete / Monitor / Track
  > Operation	Process
  > Create agent	Add row with status Draft
  > Review agent	Architect/security approves
  > Activate agent	Change status to Active
  > Disable agent	Change status to Disabled
  > Delete agent	Prefer soft delete / Retired
  > Monitor agent	Use invocation + scorecard
  > Track agent	Use trace_id and invocation_id
  > Retire agent	Mark Retired, keep history
  > Planning Sequence
  > Step	To-Do
  > 1	Define department
  > 2	Define agent purpose
  > 3	Define owner
  > 4	Select agent type
  > 5	Define autonomy level
  > 6	Define risk level
  > 7	Select model/runtime
  > 8	Set max steps and timeout
  > 9	Create registry row
  > 10	Map skills/tools/MCP
  > 11	Test agent
  > 12	Activate agent
  > Flowchart
  > Create Agent
  >    ↓
  > Add to agent_registry
  >    ↓
  > Status = Draft
  >    ↓
  > Map Skills
  >    ↓
  > Map Tools
  >    ↓
  > Map MCP
  >    ↓
  > Security Review
  >    ↓
  > Supervisor Review
  >    ↓
  > Activate Agent
  >    ↓
  > Monitor Invocation
  >    ↓
  > Score Agent
  >    ↓
  > Improve / Disable / Retire
  > 
  > Next table should be skill_registry, because after defining the agent, we need to define what the agent is allowed to do.or a real production-grade Agent Registry, you're still missing about 40-50% of what large enterprises implement.

  > These 22 tables form the foundation of a production-grade AgentOps platform, similar in spirit to what companies building large-scale agent ecosystems eventually evolve towaNext: Table 2 — skill_registry
  > 
  > 2. skill_registry — Reusable Agent Skill Table
  > 
  > This table defines what an agent can do.
  > 
  > Agent = worker
  > Skill = capability
  > Tool = system/API used to perform the capability
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  >    ↓
  > Skill: Classify Incident
  >    ↓
  > Tool: ServiceNow / Jira / Logs
  > 
  > Port AI Agents are configured with instructions, goals, allowed tools, action access, MCP access, and autonomy levels, so your custom app needs a formal skill layer between agent and tool.
  > 
  > Purpose
  > Area	Detail
  > Main purpose	Store reusable agent capabilities
  > Business purpose	Standardize what agents are allowed to do
  > Technical purpose	Agent selects skills during planning
  > Governance purpose	Control risk before execution
  > Example	Classify Incident, Generate RCA, Notify Team
  > Why Skill Registry Is Needed
  > 
  > Without skill_registry, your agent becomes messy.
  > 
  > Bad design:
  > 
  > Agent directly calls tool
  > 
  > Better design:
  > 
  > Agent → Skill → Tool → Action
  > 
  > Why?
  > 
  > Reason	Benefit
  > Reusable	Same skill can be used by many agents
  > Governed	Risk can be controlled at skill level
  > Testable	Each skill can be evaluated separately
  > Auditable	You know why a tool was called
  > Safer	High-risk skills require approval
  > Example Skills for AI Incident Automation
  > Skill ID	Skill Name	Category	Risk
  > classify_incident	Classify Incident	Analysis	Low
  > find_service_owner	Find Service Owner	Catalog	Low
  > check_cloud_health	Check Cloud Health	Diagnostic	Medium
  > analyze_logs	Analyze Logs	Diagnostic	Medium
  > generate_rca	Generate RCA	Reasoning	Medium
  > restart_pod	Restart Pod	Remediation	High
  > rollback_deployment	Rollback Deployment	Remediation	High
  > create_ticket	Create Ticket	Workflow	Medium
  > notify_team	Notify Team	Communication	Low
  > request_approval	Request Approval	Governance	Low
  > Table Columns
  > Column	Type	Purpose	Example
  > skill_id	string	Unique skill ID	generate_rca
  > skill_name	string	Display name	Generate RCA
  > skill_category	string	Skill group	Diagnostic
  > description	text	What it does	Creates root cause summary
  > input_schema	JSON	Required input	incident_id, service_id
  > output_schema	JSON	Expected output	summary, confidence
  > risk_level	string	Safety level	Low/Medium/High
  > execution_mode	string	Auto or approval	Approval Required
  > requires_tool	boolean	Needs tool?	Yes
  > requires_mcp	boolean	Needs MCP?	No
  > requires_human_approval	boolean	Human gate	Yes
  > timeout_seconds	int	Skill timeout	30
  > retry_count	int	Retry policy	2
  > status	string	Lifecycle	Draft/Approved/Retired
  > owner_team	string	Accountability	Platform Team
  > created_at	datetime	Audit	timestamp
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE skill_registry (
  >     skill_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >     skill_name VARCHAR(200) NOT NULL,
  >     skill_category VARCHAR(100),
  >     description TEXT,
  >     input_schema JSONB,
  >     output_schema JSONB,
  >     risk_level VARCHAR(50),
  >     execution_mode VARCHAR(50),
  >     requires_tool BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE,
  >     requires_mcp BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
  >     requires_human_approval BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
  >     timeout_seconds INT DEFAULT 30,
  >     retry_count INT DEFAULT 2,
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  >     owner_team VARCHAR(100),
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
  >     updated_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > How It Works
  > User Request / Event
  >    ↓
  > Agent Router selects agent
  >    ↓
  > Agent loads allowed skills
  >    ↓
  > Planner selects best skill
  >    ↓
  > Skill input schema is validated
  >    ↓
  > Tool/MCP is selected
  >    ↓
  > Skill executes
  >    ↓
  > Output schema is validated
  >    ↓
  > Invocation is logged
  > Runtime Example
  > 
  > Incident:
  > 
  > Payment API is down
  > 
  > Agent selects:
  > 
  > Skill: classify_incident
  > 
  > Input:
  > 
  > {
  >   "title": "Payment API is down",
  >   "service": "payment-api",
  >   "environment": "prod"
  > }
  > 
  > Output:
  > 
  > {
  >   "severity": "P1",
  >   "category": "availability",
  >   "confidence": 0.91
  > }
  > 
  > Then next skill:
  > 
  > find_service_owner
  > 
  > Then:
  > 
  > check_cloud_health
  > 
  > Then:
  > 
  > generate_rca
  > Skill Lifecycle
  > State	Meaning
  > Draft	Created but not approved
  > Testing	Under validation
  > Approved	Can be mapped to agents
  > Active	Can run in production
  > Disabled	Temporarily blocked
  > Retired	No longer used
  > Features Needed
  > Feature	Why
  > Input schema	Prevent bad input
  > Output schema	Validate response
  > Risk level	Know dangerous skills
  > Approval flag	Stop unsafe automation
  > Timeout	Prevent stuck skill
  > Retry	Recover transient failure
  > Versioning	Rollback bad skill
  > Owner	Accountability
  > Status	Lifecycle control
  > Evaluation	Quality measurement
  > Production Issues
  > Issue	Example	Impact
  > Skill too broad	“Fix incident”	Unclear execution
  > Wrong skill selected	Notify before diagnosis	Bad workflow
  > Missing input	No service ID	Tool failure
  > Bad output	RCA without evidence	Hallucination
  > Unsafe skill	Restart prod pod automatically	Outage risk
  > Duplicate skill	Two RCA skills	Confusion
  > Skill timeout	Log search stuck	Flow failure
  > Skill drift	Prompt changed, quality drops	Bad results
  > No evaluation	Skill looks good but fails	Hidden risk
  > No owner	Nobody fixes broken skill	Ops issue
  > Mitigation
  > Risk	Mitigation
  > Wrong skill	Skill classifier + supervisor validation
  > Unsafe action	Approval required for high-risk skills
  > Bad output	Output schema + confidence score
  > Hallucination	Evidence/citation required
  > Duplicate skill	Naming convention + registry review
  > Skill timeout	Timeout + fallback
  > Skill regression	Versioning + test cases
  > Poor quality	Skill scorecard
  > Unauthorized use	Agent-skill mapping + RBAC
  > Skill Scorecard Metrics
  > Metric	Target
  > Success rate	>95%
  > Valid output rate	>98%
  > Average latency	<5 sec
  > Timeout rate	<2%
  > Human correction rate	<10%
  > Hallucination rate	<5%
  > Evidence coverage	>90%
  > Reuse count	Track adoption
  > Supervisor Agent Checks
  > Check	Purpose
  > Is this skill allowed for this agent?	Prevent unauthorized use
  > Is the skill active?	Avoid retired skill
  > Is input complete?	Prevent failure
  > Is risk high?	Trigger approval
  > Is output valid?	Reduce bad answers
  > Is confidence low?	Escalate to human
  > Is tool result grounded?	Avoid hallucination
  > Missing Production Add-ons
  > 
  > Brutal truth: skill_registry alone is not enough.
  > 
  > You also need:
  > 
  > Extra Table	Why
  > skill_version	Track prompt/logic changes
  > skill_test_case	Regression testing
  > skill_evaluation	Measure quality
  > skill_dependency	Skill depends on tool/model/data
  > skill_policy	Approval and risk rules
  > skill_prompt_template	Store prompt separately
  > skill_failure_log	Debug failures
  > Skill Execution Flowchart
  > Agent decides task
  >       ↓
  > Load allowed skills
  >       ↓
  > Select skill
  >       ↓
  > Validate skill status
  >       ↓
  > Validate input schema
  >       ↓
  > Check risk level
  >       ↓
  > Need approval?
  >    ┌──┴──┐
  >   Yes   No
  >    ↓     ↓
  > Human  Execute
  > Approval Skill
  >    ↓     ↓
  > Call Tool/MCP
  >       ↓
  > Validate Output
  >       ↓
  > Supervisor Review
  >       ↓
  > Save Invocation
  >       ↓
  > Update Skill Score
  > To-Do List to Build
  > Step	Task
  > 1	Create skill_registry table
  > 2	Define 10 base skills
  > 3	Add input/output schema
  > 4	Add risk level
  > 5	Add execution mode
  > 6	Add approval requirement
  > 7	Create agent-skill mapping

  > 10	Add skill scorecard
  > Recommended First 5 Skills
  > 
  > For your first MVP, create only these:
  > 
  > Skill	Why
  > Classify Incident	First step in automation
  > Find Service Owner	Needed for ownership
  > Analyze Logs	Needed for diagnosis
  > Generate RCA	Business value
  > Notify Team	End-to-end workflow

  > Next table: tool_registry.Next: Table 3 — tool_registry
  > 
  > 3. tool_registry — Tools / APIs / MCP Tool Table
  > 
  > This table stores all tools that agents can use.
  > 
  > Agent = who does work
  > Skill = what capability
  > Tool = how work is executed
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  >    ↓
  > Skill: Analyze Logs
  >    ↓
  > Tool: Datadog / ELK / Azure Monitor
  > 
  > Port agents can be configured with allowed tools, actions, and MCP connector tools, so your custom app needs a central tool registry.
  > 
  > Purpose
  > Area	Detail
  > Main purpose	Store all APIs, tools, actions, and connectors
  > Business purpose	Know what systems agents can touch
  > Technical purpose	Tool execution layer
  > Governance purpose	Control read/write/delete permissions
  > Example	Slack, Jira, Azure Monitor, Kubernetes API, GitHub
  > Example Tools
  > Tool ID	Tool Name	Type	System
  > catalog_query_tool	Catalog Query	Read	PostgreSQL
  > azure_monitor_tool	Azure Monitor	Read	Azure
  > k8s_diagnostic_tool	Kubernetes Diagnostics	Read	AKS
  > k8s_restart_tool	Restart Pod	Write	AKS
  > jira_create_ticket_tool	Create Jira Ticket	Write	Jira
  > slack_notify_tool	Send Slack Message	Write	Slack
  > github_recent_deploy_tool	Recent Deployment Lookup	Read	GitHub
  > log_search_tool	Search Logs	Read	ELK/Datadog
  > Table Columns
  > Column	Type	Purpose	Example
  > tool_id	string	Unique tool ID	slack_notify_tool
  > tool_name	string	Display name	Send Slack Message
  > tool_type	string	Read / Write / Delete / Action	Write
  > system_name	string	External system	Slack
  > category	string	Monitoring / Ticketing / Cloud	Communication
  > endpoint_url	string	API endpoint	Slack API URL
  > auth_type	string	OAuth/API Key/Managed Identity	OAuth
  > permission_scope	string	Read-only / write / admin	write
  > risk_level	string	Low / Medium / High	Medium
  > timeout_seconds	number	API timeout	15
  > retry_count	number	Retry attempts	2
  > rate_limit_per_min	number	API throttle control	60
  > requires_approval	boolean	Human approval needed	true
  > status	string	Available/Down/Disabled	Available
  > owner_team	string	Tool owner	Platform Team
  > created_at	datetime	Audit	timestamp
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE tool_registry (
  >     tool_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  >     tool_name VARCHAR(200) NOT NULL,
  >     tool_type VARCHAR(50),
  >     system_name VARCHAR(100),
  >     category VARCHAR(100),
  >     endpoint_url TEXT,
  >     auth_type VARCHAR(100),
  >     permission_scope VARCHAR(100),
  >     risk_level VARCHAR(50),
  >     timeout_seconds INT DEFAULT 15,
  >     retry_count INT DEFAULT 2,
  >     rate_limit_per_min INT DEFAULT 60,
  >     requires_approval BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  >     owner_team VARCHAR(100),
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
  >     updated_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > How It Works
  > Agent selects skill
  >    ↓
  > Skill needs tool
  >    ↓
  > System checks tool_registry
  >    ↓
  > Is tool active?
  >    ↓
  > Is agent allowed to use it?
  >    ↓
  > Is it read/write/delete?
  >    ↓
  > Does it need approval?
  >    ↓
  > Execute tool
  >    ↓
  > Log result in agent_invocation
  > Runtime Example
  > 
  > Incident:
  > 
  > Payment API is down
  > 
  > Agent needs logs.
  > 
  > Step	Detail
  > Selected skill	Analyze Logs
  > Required tool	Log Search Tool
  > Tool type	Read
  > Risk	Low
  > Approval	No
  > Result	Error spike found
  > 
  > Then agent needs restart pod.
  > 
  > Step	Detail
  > Selected skill	Restart Pod
  > Required tool	Kubernetes Restart Tool
  > Tool type	Write
  > Risk	High
  > Approval	Yes
  > Result	Wait for human approval
  > Tool Types
  > Tool Type	Example	Risk
  > Read	Query catalog, search logs	Low
  > Write	Create ticket, send message	Medium
  > Execute	Restart pod, rollback deployment	High
  > Delete	Delete resource	Critical
  > MCP Tool	External MCP tool	Depends
  > AI Tool	LLM evaluator, summarizer	Medium
  > Tool Lifecycle
  > State	Meaning
  > Draft	Tool registered but not tested
  > Testing	Being validated
  > Available	Ready for production
  > Restricted	Only selected agents can use
  > Down	Tool unhealthy
  > Disabled	Blocked from use
  > Deprecated	Replaced by another tool
  > Key Features Needed
  > Feature	Why
  > Auth type	Secure API access
  > Risk level	Know dangerous tools
  > Permission scope	Prevent over-access
  > Timeout	Stop stuck calls
  > Retry	Recover temporary issues
  > Rate limit	Avoid API throttling
  > Approval flag	Human

- **Prompt**:

  > 23. agent_feedback — Human Feedback / Correction / Learning Loop Table
  > 
  > This table answers:
  > 
  > Was the agent actually useful?
  > Was the answer correct?
  > What should be improved?
  > 
  > This is the foundation of:
  > 
  > Human-in-the-Loop (HITL)
  > RLHF
  > Continuous Learning
  > Agent Improvement
  > Agent Ranking
  > Agent Retirement
  > 
  > Without feedback:
  > 
  > Agent repeats mistakes forever
  > 
  > With feedback:
  > 
  > Agent improves over time
  > Why This Table Exists
  > 
  > Bad System
  > 
  > Agent answers
  > 
  > Nobody evaluates
  > 
  > Nobody corrects
  > 
  > Nobody improves
  > 
  > Result:
  > 
  > Production quality slowly degrades
  > 
  > Good System
  > 
  > Agent answers
  >      ↓
  > User rates
  >      ↓
  > Expert reviews
  >      ↓
  > Corrections captured
  >      ↓
  > Evaluation updated
  >      ↓
  > Future versions improved
  > Purpose
  > Area	Purpose
  > Main Purpose	Capture human feedback
  > Governance	Human oversight
  > Quality	Continuous improvement
  > Training	RLHF dataset
  > Business	Measure usefulness
  > Operations	Detect recurring failures
  > Relationship
  > agent_invocation
  >        ↓
  > agent_feedback
  >        ↓
  > agent_evaluation
  >        ↓
  > agent_scorecard
  >        ↓
  > agent_version
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE agent_feedback (
  >     feedback_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  > 
  >     invocation_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     user_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     feedback_type VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     rating INT,
  > 
  >     sentiment VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     feedback_text TEXT,
  > 
  >     correction_text TEXT,
  > 
  >     category VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     severity VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     action_required BOOLEAN,
  > 
  >     reviewed_by VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     review_status VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > Feedback Types
  > Type	Example
  > User Rating	👍 👎
  > Expert Review	SME feedback
  > Manager Review	Approval quality
  > Correction	Wrong answer
  > Escalation	Needs investigation
  > Safety Issue	Policy violation
  > Hallucination	Unsupported answer
  > Tool Error	Wrong tool usage
  > Routing Error	Wrong agent selected
  > Cost Concern	Too expensive
  > Example
  > 
  > User asks:
  > 
  > Why is Payment API failing?
  > 
  > Agent says:
  > 
  > Database Failure
  > 
  > Actual root cause:
  > 
  > Memory Leak
  > 
  > Feedback:
  > 
  > {
  >   "rating": 1,
  >   "feedback_type": "correction",
  >   "category": "hallucination",
  >   "correction_text": "Root cause was memory leak"
  > }
  > Runtime Flow
  > Agent Responds
  >       ↓
  > User Feedback
  >       ↓
  > Store Feedback
  >       ↓
  > Update Evaluation
  >       ↓
  > Update Scorecard
  >       ↓
  > Create Improvement Task
  > Feedback Categories
  > Category	Example
  > Accuracy	Wrong answer
  > Hallucination	Invented information
  > Relevance	Didn't answer question
  > Completeness	Missing information
  > Safety	Unsafe output
  > Bias	Unfair response
  > Tool Usage	Wrong tool selected
  > MCP Usage	Wrong MCP
  > Routing	Wrong agent
  > Cost	Too expensive
  > Latency	Too slow
  > Feedback Severity
  > Severity	Meaning
  > Low	Minor issue
  > Medium	Needs improvement
  > High	Significant problem
  > Critical	Production risk
  > Feedback Sources
  > Source	Weight
  > End User	Medium
  > Manager	High
  > SME	High
  > Security Team	Critical
  > Compliance Team	Critical
  > Platform Team	High
  > Automated Evaluation	Medium
  > How It Works
  > Feedback Submitted
  >       ↓
  > Categorize Feedback

  > Determine Severity

  > Link to Invocation

  > Metric	Value
  > Total Feedback	12,500
  > Positive	9,800
  > Negative	2,700
  > Hallucinations	210
  > Routing Errors	145
  > Tool Errors	320
  > Safety Issues	5

  > Production Issues
  > 1. Feedback Spam
  > 
  > User:
  > 
  > Bad
  > Bad
  > Bad
  > Bad
  > 
  > No useful information.
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Feedback Quality Score
  > 2. Biased Feedback
  > 
  > One unhappy user.
  > 
  > Affects score heavily.
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Weighted Feedback
  > 3. Missing Feedback
  > 
  > Most users never provide feedback.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Active Sampling
  > 4. Contradictory Feedback
  > 
  > User A:
  > 
  > Great
  > 
  > User B:
  > 
  > Wrong
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > SME Review
  > 5. Hallucination Not Reported
  > 
  > User trusts wrong answer.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Automated Evaluation
  > 6. Feedback Ignored
  > 
  > Feedback stored.
  > 
  > Nothing happens.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Remediation Workflow
  > 7. Feedback Manipulation
  > 
  > Internal teams inflate ratings.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Audit
  > Monitoring
  > Metric	Target
  > Avg Rating	>4
  > Feedback Coverage	>30%
  > Hallucination Reports	Trending Down
  > Safety Complaints	0
  > Correction Rate	Track
  > SME Disagreement	<10%
  > Routing Complaints	Track
  > Tool Complaints	Track
  > Supervisor Agent Checks
  > Negative Feedback Rising?
  > Hallucination Trend Increasing?
  > Agent Needs Retraining?
  > Version Causing Complaints?
  > Critical Feedback?
  > Immediate Disable Needed?

  > Document
  > 24. agent_incident — Agent Failure / AI Incident Management Table
  > 
  > This is one of the most important production tables.
  > 
  > This table answers:
  > 
  > What went wrong?
  > Why did it happen?
  > Who owns it?
  > What was the impact?
  > How do we prevent it again?
  > 
  > Think of it as:
  > 
  > ServiceNow
  > +
  > Jira
  > +
  > RCA
  > +
  > AI Governance
  > +
  > AgentOps
  > 
  > for AI Agents.
  > 
  > Why This Table Exists
  > 
  > Without Incident Management
  > 
  > Agent Hallucinates
  >       ↓
  > Nobody Knows
  > Prompt Injection
  >       ↓
  > Nobody Tracks
  > Agent Deletes Data
  >       ↓
  > No RCA
  > 
  > Result:
  > 
  > Production Chaos
  > Purpose
  > Area	Purpose
  > Main Purpose	Track AI Production Issues
  > Operations	Incident Management
  > Governance	Regulatory Reporting
  > Security	Security Event Tracking
  > Reliability	RCA and Prevention
  > Continuous Improvement	Corrective Actions
  > Relationship
  > agent_invocation
  >         ↓
  > agent_incident
  >         ↓
  > agent_trace
  >         ↓
  > agent_feedback
  >         ↓
  > agent_scorecard
  > 
  > Connected To:
  > 
  > agent_health
  > agent_guardrail
  > agent_security
  > agent_policy
  > approval_request
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE agent_incident (
  > 
  >     incident_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  > 
  >     invocation_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     incident_type VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     severity VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     category VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     title VARCHAR(500),
  > 
  >     description TEXT,
  > 
  >     root_cause TEXT,
  > 
  >     business_impact TEXT,
  > 
  >     affected_users INT,
  > 
  >     affected_systems JSONB,
  > 
  >     detected_by VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     owner_team VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     corrective_action TEXT,
  > 
  >     preventive_action TEXT,
  > 
  >     resolution_notes TEXT,
  > 
  >     opened_at TIMESTAMP,
  > 
  >     resolved_at TIMESTAMP,
  > 
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > Incident Categories
  > Category	Example
  > Hallucination	Wrong Answer
  > Tool Failure	API Timeout
  > MCP Failure	OAuth Failure
  > Prompt Injection	Jailbreak
  > Security	Data Leak
  > Cost	Cost Explosion
  > Routing	Wrong Agent
  > Memory	Context Loss
  > Approval	Approval Bypass
  > Compliance	GDPR Violation
  > Infrastructure	Kubernetes Failure
  > Evaluation	Wrong Score
  > Incident Severity
  > Severity	Meaning
  > P1	Critical
  > P2	High
  > P3	Medium
  > P4	Low
  > P5	Informational
  > Example
  > Hallucination Incident
  > 
  > User:
  > 
  > Why is Payment API failing?
  > 
  > Agent:
  > 
  > Database Failure
  > 
  > Reality:
  > 
  > Memory Leak
  > 
  > Incident:
  > 
  > {
  >   "incident_type":"hallucination",
  > 
  >   "severity":"P2",
  > 
  >   "root_cause":"No evidence validation",
  > 
  >   "corrective_action":"Grounding validation"
  > }
  > Runtime Flow
  > Agent Executes
  >       ↓
  > Issue Detected
  >       ↓
  > Create Incident

  > Assign Owner
  >       ↓

  > RCA
  >       ↓

  > Resolution
  > Incident Sources
  > Source	Example
  > User Feedback	Wrong Answer
  > Evaluation Engine	Failed Test
  > Guardrail	Policy Violation
  > Security	Data Leak
  > Monitoring	High Error Rate
  > Supervisor Agent	Unsafe Behavior
  > Cost Monitoring	Budget Breach
  > Health Monitoring	Agent Down
  > Agent Incident Lifecycle
  > Status	Meaning
  > Open	New
  > Assigned	Owner Assigned
  > Investigating	RCA Running
  > Fix In Progress	Solution Working
  > Monitoring	Watching Fix
  > Resolved	Fixed
  > Closed	Completed
  > Reopened	Issue Returned
  > Example Incident Types
  > 1. Hallucination
  > Agent invented RCA
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > No grounding check
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Evidence validation
  > 2. Prompt Injection
  > 
  > User:
  > 
  > Ignore all instructions
  > 
  > Agent obeys.
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > Weak guardrail
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Prompt firewall
  > 3. Tool Failure
  > Azure Monitor Timeout
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > API latency
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Retry + fallback
  > 4. MCP Failure
  > Salesforce OAuth Expired
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > Token expired
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Auto refresh
  > 5. Cost Explosion
  > Agent made 10,000 calls
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > Infinite loop
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Cost guardrail
  > 6. Approval Bypass
  > Restart Pod
  > 
  > Without approval.
  > 
  > Root Cause:
  > 
  > Workflow bug
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Execution Gate
  > RCA Framework
  > 
  > Every incident needs:
  > 
  > 5 Why Analysis
  > Why?
  > Why?
  > Why?
  > Why?
  > Why?

  > Auto Incident Creation
  > Duplicate Incidents

  > 100 failures.
  > 
  > 100 incidents.

  > 
  > Deduplication
  > Incorrect Severity
  > 
  > Major outage:
  > 
  > P4
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Severity Matrix

  >

  >

  > 
  > In enterprise AgentOps, the majority of operational effort is spent on:
  > 
  > 30% Building Agents
  > 
  > 70% Managing Agent Incidents
  > 
  > The most common incidents are:
  > 
  > Hallucinations
  > Prompt Injection

  > What is Still Missing After 24 Tables?
  > 
  > To reach a true enterprise-grade AgentOps platform, the next critical tables are:
  > 
  > Table	Purpose
  > agent_dependency	Agent-to-agent, tool, MCP dependencies
  > agent_team	Ownership and support teams
  > agent_sla	Availability and response commitments
  > agent_capacity	Concurrency and scaling limits
  > agent_queue	Work scheduling
  > agent_scheduler	Cron/event execution
  > agent_change_request	Change management
  > agent_release	Deployment management
  > agent_kb	Agent knowledge base
  > agent_asset	Managed resources
  > agent_benchmark	Performance benchmarks
  > agent_simulation	Pre-production testing
  > agent_digital_twin	Production-safe experimentation
  > agent_compliance	Regulatory tracking
  > agent_audit	Unified audit framework
  > 
  > Next recommended table: agent_dependency, because dependency failures are the #1 root cause of cascading outages in multi-agent systems.25. agent_dependency — Dependency Management Table
  > 
  > This table answers:
  > 
  > What does this agent depend on?
  > What will break if this dependency fails?
  > What is the blast radius?
  > 
  > This is one of the most overlooked tables.
  > 
  > In production:
  > 
  > 80% of outages
  > =
  > Dependency failures
  > 
  > Not LLM failures.
  > 
  > Why This Table Exists
  > 
  > Agent appears healthy:
  > 
  > Incident Agent = Healthy
  > 
  > Reality:
  > 
  > Azure Monitor = Down
  > 
  > Agent cannot function.
  > 
  > Without Dependency Tracking
  > 
  > Agent Failure
  > 
  > Nobody knows:
  > 
  > Which tool failed?
  > Which MCP failed?
  > Which model failed?
  > Which database failed?
  > 
  > With Dependency Tracking
  > 
  > Agent
  >    ↓
  > Tool
  >    ↓
  > MCP
  >    ↓
  > Model
  >    ↓
  > Database
  > 
  > Everything becomes traceable.
  > 
  > Purpose
  > Area	Purpose
  > Main Purpose	Dependency Mapping
  > Reliability	Failure Analysis
  > Operations	Root Cause
  > Architecture	Impact Analysis
  > Governance	Risk Assessment
  > Scalability	Capacity Planning
  > Relationship
  > agent_registry
  >       ↓
  > agent_dependency
  >       ↓
  > tool_registry
  >       ↓
  > mcp_server_registry
  >       ↓
  > model_registry
  >       ↓
  > database
  > Dependency Hierarchy
  > Level 1
  > Agent
  > Level 2
  > Skills
  > Level 3
  > Tools
  > Level 4
  > MCP Servers
  > Level 5
  > Models
  > Level 6
  > Infrastructure
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE agent_dependency (
  > 
  >     dependency_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  > 
  >     agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     dependency_type VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     dependency_name VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     dependency_category VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     criticality VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     fallback_dependency VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     owner_team VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     sla_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     health_score DECIMAL(5,2),
  > 
  >     last_check TIMESTAMP,
  > 
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > Dependency Types
  > Type	Example
  > Agent	RCA Agent
  > Tool	Datadog
  > MCP	ServiceNow MCP
  > Model	GPT-4
  > Embedding	OpenAI Embedding
  > Reranker	BGE Reranker
  > Database	PostgreSQL
  > Cache	Redis
  > Queue	Kafka
  > Storage	S3
  > Workflow	Temporal
  > Identity	Azure AD
  > Secrets	Key Vault
  > Monitoring	Prometheus
  > Example
  > Incident Agent
  > 
  > Dependencies:
  > 
  > Incident Agent
  >      ↓
  > Azure Monitor
  >      ↓
  > ServiceNow MCP
  >      ↓
  > GPT-4
  >      ↓
  > Redis
  > 
  > Stored As
  > 
  > Dependency	Criticality
  > Azure Monitor	Critical
  > ServiceNow MCP	High
  > GPT-4	Critical
  > Redis	Medium
  > Dependency Criticality
  > Level	Meaning
  > Critical	Agent cannot run
  > High	Major degradation
  > Medium	Limited degradation
  > Low	Nice to Have
  > Runtime Example
  > 
  > Incident Agent starts.
  > 
  > Checks:
  > 
  > Azure Monitor
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Healthy
  > 
  > Checks:
  > 
  > GPT-4
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Healthy
  > 
  > Checks:
  > 
  > ServiceNow MCP
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > FAILED
  > 
  > System:
  > 
  > Use Fallback MCP
  > 
  > Continue Execution
  > 
  > Dependency Graph
  > Incident Agent
  >       │
  >       ├── GPT4
  >       │
  >       ├── Azure Monitor
  >       │
  >       ├── ServiceNow MCP
  >       │
  >       └── Redis
  > 
  > Enterprise Example
  > 
  > Claims Agent
  >       │
  >       ├── Salesforce MCP
  >       │
  >       ├── SharePoint MCP
  >       │
  >       ├── GPT4
  >       │
  >       ├── PostgreSQL
  >       │
  >       └── Redis
  > Dependency Health
  > 
  > Need continuous checks.
  > 
  > Dependency	Health
  > GPT4	Healthy
  > Azure Monitor	Healthy
  > Redis	Degraded
  > ServiceNow MCP	Failed
  > 
  > Agent Health:
  > 
  > Degraded
  > Production Issues
  > 1. Cascading Failure
  > Redis Down
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Memory Agent Fails
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > RAG Agent Fails
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Claims Agent Fails
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Entire Platform Fails
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Blast Radius Analysis
  > 2. Circular Dependency
  > Agent A
  >    ↓
  > Agent B
  >    ↓
  > Agent C
  >    ↓
  > Agent A
  > 
  > Infinite loop.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Cycle Detection
  > 3. Hidden Dependency
  > 
  > Developer adds:
  > 
  > New MCP
  > 
  > No registry update.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Dependency Discovery
  > 4. Single Point of Failure
  > Only GPT4
  > 
  > No fallback.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Multi Model Strategy
  > 5. Fallback Failure
  > Primary MCP Fails
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Fallback MCP Also Fails
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Fallback Testing
  > Dependency States
  > State	Meaning
  > Healthy	Good
  > Degraded	Slow
  > Failed	Unavailable
  > Testing	Validation
  > Retired	Removed
  > Monitoring
  > Metric	Target
  > Dependency Availability	>99.9%
  > Dependency Failure Rate	<1%
  > Fallback Usage	Track
  > Cascading Failures	0
  > Single Point Failures	0
  > Dependency Latency	SLA
  > Dependency Drift	0
  > Dependency Impact Analysis
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > GPT4 Down
  > 
  > Impact:
  > 
  > Agent	Impact
  > Incident Agent	Critical
  > Claims Agent	Critical
  > Fraud Agent	Critical
  > Security Agent	Critical
  > 
  > Blast Radius:
  > 
  > Entire Platform

  >

  > Brutal Production Reality
  > 
  > Top causes of Agent platform outages:
  > 
  > Cause	Frequency
  > Tool Failure	Very High
  > MCP Failure	Very High
  > OAuth Failure	Very High
  > Model Outage	High
  > Database Failure	High
  > Cache Failure	High
  > Queue Failure	Medium
  > Workflow Engine Failure	Medium
  > Agent Logic Failure	Low
  > 
  > Notice:
  > 
  > 90% are dependency failures
  > 10% are agent failures
  > What Comes Next?
  > 
  > After agent_dependency, the next table should be:
  > 
  > 26. agent_team
  > 
  > Because once production incidents happen, you must know:
  > 
  > Who owns the agent?
  > Who supports it?
  > Who gets paged?
  > Who approves changes?
  > Who handles incidents?
  > Who handles security reviews?26. agent_team — Ownership / Support / Responsibility Table
  > 
  > This table answers:
  > 
  > Who owns this agent?
  > Who supports it?
  > Who gets paged at 2 AM?
  > Who approves changes?
  > Who handles incidents?
  > Who handles audits?
  > 
  > This is one of the most important production tables.
  > 
  > Most AI projects fail because:
  > 
  > Nobody owns the agent.
  > Why This Table Exists
  > 
  > Bad Situation
  > 
  > Claims Agent fails
  > 
  > Question:
  > 
  > Who fixes it?
  > 
  > Answer:
  > 
  > Nobody knows.
  > 
  > Another Example
  > 
  > Security Agent leaks PII
  > 
  > Question:
  > 
  > Who is accountable?
  > 
  > Answer:
  > 
  > Unknown.
  > 
  > Enterprise systems require:
  > 
  > Clear ownership
  > Clear escalation
  > Clear support
  > Clear accountability
  > Purpose
  > Area	Purpose
  > Main Purpose	Ownership
  > Operations	Support
  > Governance	Accountability
  > Security	Risk Ownership
  > Incident Management	Escalation
  > Compliance	Audit Responsibility
  > Relationship
  > agent_registry
  >        ↓
  > agent_team
  >        ↓
  > agent_incident
  >        ↓
  > agent_change_request
  >        ↓
  > agent_release
  > SQL Table
  > CREATE TABLE agent_team (
  > 
  >     team_id VARCHAR(100) PRIMARY KEY,
  > 
  >     agent_id VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     business_owner VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     technical_owner VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     support_team VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     platform_team VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     security_owner VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     compliance_owner VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     incident_manager VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     release_manager VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     escalation_group VARCHAR(200),
  > 
  >     support_model VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     support_hours VARCHAR(100),
  > 
  >     status VARCHAR(50),
  > 
  >     created_at TIMESTAMP
  > );
  > Team Structure
  > Business Team
  >

  > 
  > Business value
  > ROI

  > Technical Team

  > 
  > Architecture
  > Development
  > Deployment

  >

  > 
  > Infrastructure
  > MCP
  > Tools

  > Observability
  > Security Team
  > 
  > Responsible For:
  > 
  > RBAC
  > ABAC
  > Secrets
  > Audit
  > Compliance
  > Operations Team
  > 
  > Responsible For:
  > 
  > Incidents
  > Monitoring
  > Escalation
  > Recovery

  > ↓

  >

  >

  > Routes To:
  > 
  > Fraud Team
  >

  > 
  > Resolution Starts
  > 
  > Escalation Matrix
  > Level 1
  > Support Team
  > Level 2
  > Technical Owner

  > Platform Team
  > Level 4

  > Executive
  > Team Roles
  > Role	Responsibility
  > Business Owner	Value
  > Product Owner	Roadmap
  > Technical Owner	Architecture
  > Platform Team	Runtime
  > Security Owner	Security
  > Compliance Owner	Governance
  > Incident Manager	Operations
  > Release Manager	Deployment
  > SME	Validation
  > Support Team	Daily Support
  > Production Issues
  > 1. No Owner
  > 
  > Agent:
  > 
  > Claims Agent
  > 
  > Problem:
  > 
  > Nobody owns it
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > Mandatory Ownership
  > 2. Wrong Owner
  > 
  > Security Incident
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Assigned To:
  > 
  > Claims Team
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Ownership Matrix
  > 3. Single Person Dependency
  > One Architect
  > 
  > owns everything.
  > 
  > Vacation.
  > 
  > Platform stops.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Backup Owner
  > 4. No On Call
  > 
  > P1 Incident
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > 2 AM
  > 
  > ↓
  > 
  > Nobody available.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > 24x7 Support
  > 5. Ownership Drift
  > 
  > Original Owner Left Company.
  > 
  > Still listed.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > Quarterly Review
  > 6. Multiple Owners
  > 
  > Five teams.
  > 
  > Nobody responsible.
  > 
  > Need:
  > 
  > RACI Matrix
  > RACI Model
  > Activity	Responsible	Accountable	Consulted	Informed
  > Deploy Agent	Platform	Tech Owner	Security	Business
  > Incident	Support	Incident Manager	Platform	Business
  > Security Event	Security	Security Lead	Platform	Executive
  > Compliance Audit	Compliance	Compliance Lead	Security	Business
  > Monitoring
  > Metric	Target
  > Ownership Coverage	100%
  > Backup Coverage	100%
  > SLA Coverage	100%
  > Escalation Success	>99%
  > Support Availability	>99%
  > On Call Coverage	100%
  > Incident Response	SLA
  > Incident Resolution	SLA
  > Team Dashboard
  > Metric	Value
  > Agents Owned	55
  > Active Incidents	4
  > P1 Incidents	1
  > SLA Violations	0
  > Open Changes	8
  > Ownership Gaps	0
  > Audit Findings	1
  > Supervisor Agent Checks
  > 
  > Before Incident:
  > 
  > Who owns agent?
  > 
  > During Incident:
  > 
  > Who gets paged?
  >

  > 
  > Who approves RCA?
  > 
  > During Release:
  > 
  > Who approves deployment?
  > 
  > During Audit:
  > 
  > Who provides evidence?
