## 2026-06-10T23:48:47.003212+00:00 · 4e46ee31
- **Source**: claude_code
- **Category**: user
- **Session**: 2026-06-10
- **Prompt**:

  > Global Policy + Status + Notification + Plan
  > 1. Global AI Project Policy
  > Policy Area	Global Rule
  > Naming	No hardcoded project, folder, agent, model, or environment name
  > Config	Everything must come from config/env/registry
  > Prompt	Every prompt must be logged, versioned, reviewed
  > Agent	Every agent must have owner, role, permission, version
  > MCP/Tool	Every tool must have schema, auth, timeout, audit
  > Data	Every data source must have owner, ACL, lineage, freshness
  > RAG	Every answer needs citation, source, index version
  > Text2SQL	SQL must be validated before execution
  > Model	Model must be registered, benchmarked, monitored
  > API	API must have version, auth, rate limit, trace ID
  > UI	UI must show status, trace, error, review, approval
  > Testing	Regression + security + performance tests required
  > Monitoring	Logs, metrics, traces, cost, quality required
  > Recovery	Checkpoint, retry, resume, rollback required
  > Release	Dev → QA → UAT → Prod approval required
  > 2. Global Workflow Status
  > Status	Meaning
  > CREATED	request received
  > LOGGED	prompt saved
  > PLANNED	task plan created
  > IN_PROGRESS	agents running
  > WAITING_APPROVAL	human approval needed
  > BLOCKED	dependency/error stopping progress
  > RETRYING	retry in progress
  > FAILED	workflow failed
  > RECOVERING	restarting from checkpoint
  > COMPLETED	final output done
  > CANCELLED	stopped by user/admin
  > ROLLED_BACK	reverted to previous safe state
  > 3. Status Update Format
  > 
  > Every status update should include:
  > 
  > Project:
  > Workflow ID:
  > Department:
  > Current Status:
  > Current Step:
  > Owner:
  > Progress:
  > Blocker:
  > Risk:
  > Next Action:
  > ETA / Target:
  > Last Updated By:
  > Last Updated At:
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Project: AI Claims Assistant
  > Workflow ID: WF-10045
  > Department: Claims
  > Current Status: WAITING_APPROVAL
  > Current Step: Reviewer Agent Validation
  > Owner: Claims Manager
  > Progress: 75%
  > Blocker: Human approval needed
  > Risk: Medium
  > Next Action: Approve generated claim summary
  > Last Updated By: supervisor_agent
  > Last Updated At: 2026-06-10 14:30 MST
  > 4. Notification Policy
  > Event	Notify Whom	Channel
  > Workflow created	requester	UI / email
  > Plan created	requester + owner	UI
  > Approval needed	approver	email / Teams / Slack
  > Workflow failed	support + owner	Teams / incident
  > Retry started	support	UI
  > Retry failed	support + tech owner	Teams
  > High-risk output	reviewer + compliance	email
  > PII detected	security	incident alert
  > Cost spike	FinOps + admin	dashboard/email
  > SLA breach	support manager	incident alert
  > Production issue	incident team	PagerDuty/Teams
  > Completed	requester	UI/email
  > Rollback done	owner + admin	Teams/email
  > 5. Notification Message Template
  > Title: [Status] Workflow WF-10045 requires approval
  > 
  > Project: AI Claims Assistant
  > Department: Claims
  > Status: WAITING_APPROVAL
  > Current Step: Human Review
  > Risk Level: Medium
  > Reason: Confidence score below threshold
  > Action Needed: Approve / Reject / Send Back
  > Owner: Claims Manager
  > Time: 2026-06-10 14:30 MST
  > Trace ID: TRC-88991
  > 6. Global Execution Plan
  > Phase	Work
  > Phase 1	Create policy, naming, config, registry standards
  > Phase 2	Build prompt logging and workflow status tables
  > Phase 3	Add agent registry, skill registry, MCP registry
  > Phase 4	Add status dashboard in UI
  > Phase 5	Add notification engine
  > Phase 6	Add approval workflow
  > Phase 7	Add error, retry, checkpoint, resume
  > Phase 8	Add observability: logs, metrics, traces
  > Phase 9	Add testing and benchmark dashboard
  > Phase 10	Add release gate and rollback process
  > 7. Database Tables Needed
  > Table	Purpose
  > workflow_run	main workflow status
  > workflow_step	step-by-step agent execution
  > prompt_log	all user prompts
  > agent_registry	all agents
  > tool_registry	APIs/MCP tools
  > model_registry	models used
  > notification_log	sent notifications
  > approval_request	human approval
  > error_log	failures
  > checkpoint_store	resume after crash
  > audit_log	full audit trail
  > status_history	every status change
  > 8. UI Dashboard
  > UI Tab	Shows
  > Overview	total workflows, success, failure
  > Status	current status by department
  > Plan	workflow steps and owner
  > Notifications	sent/pending alerts
  > Approvals	pending human actions
  > Errors	failed workflows
  > Recovery	retry/resume/rollback
  > Agents	agent health and usage
  > Testing	pass/fail/benchmark
  > Audit	full history
  > 9. Final Rule
  > 
  > Every workflow must be:
  > 
  > Logged
  > Planned
  > Status-tracked
  > Notified
  > Reviewed
  > Tested
  > Audited
  > Recoverable
  > Rollback-ready
  > 
  > Without this, you cannot manage a production AI platforYou already have ~80% of the list. The remaining 20% are the items that usually cause production incidents, audit findings, or expensive rework.
  > 
  > 1. Knowledge Transfer & Maintainability
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > Bus factor = 1	Only one person understands system
  > Missing onboarding guide	New developers struggle
  > Missing architecture glossary	Different teams use different terms
  > Missing domain model	Business concepts unclear
  > Tribal knowledge	Information only in meetings
  > No ownership map	Nobody knows who owns what
  > 2. AI Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No AI usage policy	Uncontrolled adoption
  > No model approval process	Random model selection
  > No prompt approval workflow	Unsafe prompts
  > No AI risk classification	Same controls for all use cases
  > No AI inventory	Unknown AI systems in company
  > No model retirement process	Old models still running
  > No Responsible AI review	Bias/compliance issues
  > 3. Agent Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No agent lifecycle	Orphan agents
  > No agent certification	Unverified agents in production
  > No agent KPI	Cannot measure usefulness
  > No agent retirement policy	Dead agents remain active
  > No agent ownership	Nobody fixes issues
  > No agent dependency graph	Hidden coupling
  > 4. MCP Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No MCP inventory	Unknown integrations
  > No MCP SLA	Tool reliability unknown
  > No MCP version management	Breaking changes
  > No MCP approval workflow	Unsafe tools exposed
  > No MCP sandbox testing	Production failures
  > No MCP security review	Data leakage
  > 5. Data Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No data steward	No accountability
  > No master data strategy	Duplicate entities
  > No reference data management	Inconsistent values
  > No lineage validation	Traceability issues
  > No data contracts	Producer/consumer mismatch
  > No archival strategy	Storage explosion
  > 6. RAG Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No source certification	Untrusted documents
  > No freshness scoring	Stale answers
  > No document expiration	Old policies returned
  > No duplicate detection	Retrieval confusion
  > No retrieval benchmark	Unknown quality
  > No citation audit	False references
  > 7. Fine-Tuning Governance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No training data approval	Garbage training
  > No drift detection	Quality degradation
  > No retraining schedule	Model becomes outdated
  > No model card	Missing documentation
  > No bias review	Fairness issues
  > No benchmark comparison	Cannot justify model choice
  > 8. LLMOps Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No prompt version control	Inconsistent outputs
  > No prompt rollback	Bad prompt stays live
  > No A/B testing	No optimization
  > No shadow deployment	Risky releases
  > No canary release	Large outages
  > No model routing strategy	High cost
  > 9. Security Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No threat modeling	Unknown vulnerabilities
  > No penetration testing	Hidden security flaws
  > No secret rotation	Credential compromise
  > No key management policy	Weak encryption
  > No data masking	Sensitive exposure
  > No insider threat controls	Internal abuse
  > 10. Compliance Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No audit evidence	Compliance failure
  > No retention policy	Legal issues
  > No deletion workflow	Privacy violation
  > No consent management	Regulatory breach
  > No legal hold process	Discovery problems
  > No compliance reporting	Audit failure
  > 11. Operational Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No runbooks	Slow recovery
  > No incident command process	Chaos during outage
  > No escalation matrix	Delayed response
  > No support model	User frustration
  > No shift handover process	Lost context
  > No operational calendar	Conflicting changes
  > 12. Disaster Recovery Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No RTO defined	Unknown recovery expectations
  > No RPO defined	Unknown data loss tolerance
  > No DR testing	False confidence
  > No backup validation	Corrupt backups
  > No multi-region strategy	Large outage impact
  > No failback plan	Recovery complications
  > 13. Financial / FinOps Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No token budget	Cost explosion
  > No cost allocation	Cannot charge departments
  > No cloud budget alerts	Unexpected bills
  > No ROI measurement	Hard to justify investment
  > No cost forecasting	Budget overruns
  > No model cost optimization	Wasteful usage
  > 14. Business Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No business KPI	Technical success, business failure
  > No adoption tracking	Low usage
  > No stakeholder map	Missing requirements
  > No value realization tracking	ROI unclear
  > No change management	Resistance to adoption
  > No communication plan	User confusion
  > 15. Architecture Artifacts Often Missing
  > Artifact	Why Important
  > ADR (Architecture Decision Records)	Why decisions were made
  > NFR Catalog	Performance/security/scalability requirements
  > Dependency Map	Understand system coupling
  > Data Flow Diagram	Security and compliance
  > Threat Model	Security planning
  > RACI Matrix	Ownership clarity
  > Service Catalog	Discoverability
  > Capability Map	Business alignment
  > Environment Matrix	Dev/Test/Prod consistency
  > Release Calendar	Coordination
  > 16. AI Evaluation Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No benchmark dataset	Cannot measure quality
  > No hallucination tracking	Hidden errors
  > No citation accuracy metric	Trust issues
  > No grounding metric	Unsupported answers
  > No user satisfaction score	Poor adoption
  > No business outcome metric	No ROI evidence
  > 17. Human-in-the-Loop Gaps
  > Missing Area	Risk
  > No approval thresholds	Inconsistent reviews
  > No reviewer training	Poor decisions
  > No feedback capture	No improvement
  > No escalation rules	Delays
  > No review audit trail	Compliance risk
  > No correction workflow	Errors persist
  > Final Enterprise Checklist
  > 
  > For a production-grade:
  > 
  > Multi-Agent + MCP + RAG + Text2SQL + Fine-Tuning + API + Frontend + Ollama + Hyperscaler
  > 
  > you ultimately need governance across:
  > 
  > People
  > Process
  > Technology
  > Data
  > Model
  > Prompt
  > Agent
  > Tool
  > Security
  > Compliance
  > Operations
  > Recovery
  > Cost
  > Testing
  > Observability
  > Business Value
  > 
  > Most teams build the technology and forget the governance, ownership, recovery, and operational layers. Those are usually what determine whether the platform survives beyond the first successful demThis is one of the biggest production risks with AI-assisted development.
  > 
  > People focus on hallucination, but in real projects AI creates many more subtle problems.
  > 
  > 1. Coding Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Hallucinated APIs	Method doesn't exist
  > Hallucinated libraries	Fake package names
  > Wrong SDK version	Uses deprecated syntax
  > Missing error handling	No try/catch
  > Hardcoded values	URLs, passwords, project names
  > Missing security validation	SQL injection risk
  > Race condition	Concurrent update issue
  > Memory leak	Objects not released
  > Duplicate code	Similar logic everywhere
  > Circular dependency	Module import loop
  > Wrong retry logic	Infinite retry
  > Missing timeout	Service hangs
  > Missing idempotency	Duplicate transaction
  > Wrong transaction handling	Partial data commit
  > Incorrect business logic	Compiles but wrong result
  > 2. README Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Missing prerequisites	Cannot run project
  > Wrong install steps	Build fails
  > Missing environment variables	Startup failure
  > Outdated architecture	Doesn't match code
  > Wrong API examples	Users confused
  > Missing troubleshooting	Support burden
  > Missing rollback procedure	Recovery impossible
  > Missing security notes	Vulnerability risk
  > Missing dependency list	Deployment issue
  > Missing ownership	Nobody maintains
  > 3. Architecture Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Overengineering	50 agents for simple workflow
  > Missing scalability	Works for 10 users only
  > Missing HA	Single point of failure
  > Missing DR	No disaster recovery
  > Missing security boundary	Cross-tenant data leak
  > Wrong service decomposition	Too many microservices
  > Tight coupling	Services depend on each other
  > Missing observability	Cannot troubleshoot
  > Missing governance	No approval flow
  > Vendor lock-in	Difficult migration
  > Missing cost controls	Cloud bill explosion
  > 4. Status Update Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > False progress	"80% done" not true
  > Missing blockers	Management unaware
  > Missing risks	Project surprises
  > Missing dependencies	Hidden delays
  > No confidence level	Unrealistic estimates
  > Generated generic updates	No real value
  > 5. Agent Creation Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Too many agents	Complexity explosion
  > Agent overlap	Same task twice
  > Infinite loops	Agent A → Agent B → Agent A
  > No ownership	Nobody responsible
  > Wrong routing	Incorrect agent selected
  > Missing escalation	Human never involved
  > Missing state tracking	Cannot resume
  > Missing versioning	Behavior changes unexpectedly
  > 6. Monitoring Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Monitoring everything	High cost
  > Monitoring nothing useful	Miss critical failures
  > No business KPI	Only technical metrics
  > No alerts	Nobody notified
  > Alert fatigue	Too many alerts
  > Missing SLA tracking	Performance unknown
  > 7. Error Monitoring Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Logs only	No root cause
  > Missing correlation ID	Can't trace request
  > Missing stack trace	Hard debugging
  > Silent failures	Errors hidden
  > No severity classification	Everything same priority
  > No incident ownership	Nobody fixes
  > 8. Testing Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Missing edge cases	Production failures
  > Happy path only	Unrealistic testing
  > No regression tests	Old features break
  > Fake test coverage	Tests don't verify business logic
  > No load testing	Performance collapse
  > No security testing	Vulnerabilities missed
  > No chaos testing	Recovery untested
  > 9. API Design Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Inconsistent naming	Confusing APIs
  > Missing versioning	Breaking changes
  > Missing rate limits	Abuse possible
  > No pagination	Large response failure
  > Poor error messages	Debugging difficult
  > Missing auth checks	Security issue
  > Wrong HTTP codes	Client confusion
  > 10. Output Generation Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Hallucinated facts	False information
  > Missing citations	Cannot verify
  > Wrong calculations	Business impact
  > Missing context	Bad decision
  > Overconfident answers	High risk
  > Outdated information	Wrong recommendations
  > 11. Flowchart Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Missing decision nodes	Logic incomplete
  > Missing exception paths	Unrealistic workflow
  > Missing approvals	Governance gap
  > Wrong sequence	Execution failure
  > No retry path	Recovery impossible
  > Missing fallback	Workflow breaks
  > 12. Sequence Diagram Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Missing actor	Incomplete flow
  > Wrong order	Invalid design
  > Missing async events	Kafka/EventHub ignored
  > Missing timeout	Hanging requests
  > Missing retries	No resiliency
  > Missing failure path	Unrealistic diagram
  > 13. C4 Model Mistakes
  > Level	Common Mistake
  > Context	Missing external systems
  > Container	Wrong boundaries
  > Component	Too much detail
  > Code	Outdated diagrams
  > All Levels	Missing security/data flow
  > 14. Network Diagram Mistakes
  > Issue	Example
  > Missing firewall rules	Security gap
  > Missing VNET/VPC	Network confusion
  > Missing load balancer	SPOF
  > Missing DR region	Disaster risk
  > Missing DNS flow	Routing issues
  > Missing ingress/egress	Security exposure
  > 15. Multi-Agent + MCP + RAG Specific Mistakes
  > Issue	Impact
  > Wrong tool selected	Incorrect output
  > Wrong document retrieved	Hallucination
  > Wrong chunking strategy	Poor recall
  > Wrong embedding model	Low relevance
  > MCP schema mismatch	Runtime failure
  > Agent memory pollution	Wrong decisions
  > Context overflow	Lost information
  > Tool timeout	Workflow failure
  > Prompt injection	Security breach
  > Citation mismatch	Trust issue
  > 16. Missing Production Artifacts (Most Common)
  > 
  > AI frequently forgets to create:
  > 
  > Architecture Decision Records (ADR)
  > Runbooks
  > Operational Playbooks
  > Incident Management Procedures
  > Disaster Recovery Plans
  > Capacity Planning Documents
  > Security Threat Models
  > Data Lineage Diagrams
  > SLA/SLO Definitions
  > RACI Matrix
  > Release Checklist
  > Rollback Checklist
  > UAT Signoff
  > Performance Benchmark Reports
  > Cost Forecast Reports
  > Compliance Evidence
  > The Biggest AI Mistake
  > 
  > The most dangerous issue is:
  > 
  > Everything looks correct.
  > Everything compiles.
  > Everything deploys.
  > 
  > But the business logic is wrong.
  > 
  > This is why every AI-generated artifact (code, architecture, API, flowchart, sequence diagram, C4 model, README, monitoring setup) should pass:
  > 
  > Human Review
  > +
  > Automated Testing
  > +
  > Architecture Review
  > +
  > Security Review
  > +
  > Business Validation
  > +
  > Benchmark Validation
  > 
  > before being considered production-ready.Token Saving Policy + Use Ollama More
  > 1. Token Saving Policy
  > Area	Policy
  > Prompt	keep short, structured, no repeated history
  > Context	send only relevant chunks, not full documents
  > Memory	summarize old conversation every few turns
  > RAG	top 3–5 chunks only, not top 20
  > Agent Loop	max agent steps, max retries
  > Output	define short/medium/long response mode
  > Logs	store full logs in DB, send summary to model
  > Code	send only changed files/diff, not full repo
  > Testing	send failed tests only, not all passed tests
  > Review	reviewer checks final output + evidence only
  > Retry	retry with smaller context first
  > Cache	reuse same prompt/output when unchanged
  > 2. Use Ollama More Policy
  > Task	Use Ollama Local
  > Prompt cleanup	yes
  > Prompt classification	yes
  > Intent detection	yes
  > Simple planning	yes
  > Log summarization	yes
  > Error explanation	yes
  > Test case draft	yes
  > Code review first pass	yes
  > Documentation draft	yes
  > Feedback classification	yes
  > RAG query rewrite	yes
  > PII pre-check	yes
  > 
  > Use paid/cloud model only for:
  > 
  > Task	Use Cloud Model
  > complex reasoning	
  > final high-risk answer	
  > legal/finance/HR approval	
  > production code generation	
  > architecture decision	
  > customer-facing output	
  > low-confidence local output	
  > 3. Routing Policy
  > Input Prompt
  >   ↓
  > Small Ollama model:
  > - classify intent
  > - detect risk
  > - summarize context
  > - remove duplicates
  >   ↓
  > If simple:
  >   use Ollama
  >   ↓
  > If complex/high-risk:
  >   use cloud model
  >   ↓
  > Reviewer:
  >   Ollama first
  >   cloud reviewer only if confidence low
  > 4. Token Budget by Step
  > Step	Max Token Policy
  > Prompt classification	300–500 tokens
  > Planning	800–1,500 tokens
  > RAG retrieval context	2,000–4,000 tokens
  > Code review	changed diff only
  > Final answer	based on user mode
  > Reviewer	final output + source only
  > Log analysis	last 100–300 lines only
  > Error debugging	stack trace + related config only
  > 5. Model Selection
  > Task	Ollama Model
  > fast classification	phi3, gemma2:2b
  > normal reasoning	llama3.1:8b, mistral
  > code	qwen2.5-coder, deepseek-coder
  > summarization	gemma2, llama3.1
  > security first pass	llama3.1, mistral
  > 6. Database Tracking
  > 
  > Track token/cost every run:
  > 
  > Table	Fields
  > model_run	model, provider, input_tokens, output_tokens
  > cost_log	request_id, user_id, department, cost
  > cache_log	prompt_hash, cache_hit, saved_tokens
  > routing_log	local_model_used, cloud_model_used, reason
  > budget_policy	max_tokens, max_cost, escalation_rule
  > 7. Token Saving Techniques
  > Technique	Benefit
  > prompt compression	smaller input
  > context pruning	remove irrelevant text
  > semantic cache	avoid repeated calls
  > response cache	reuse same answer
  > RAG chunk filtering	fewer chunks
  > reranking before LLM	better context
  > conversation summary	avoid full history
  > diff-based code review	huge saving
  > batch small tasks	fewer calls
  > stop sequences	prevent long output
  > 8. UI Dashboard
  > 
  > Show:
  > 
  > Token Used Today
  > Cost Saved by Ollama
  > Cloud Calls Avoided
  > Cache Hit Rate
  > Most Expensive Workflows
  > Agent Token Usage
  > Department Token Usage
  > Failed High-Cost Runs
  > 9. Brutal Rule
  > 
  > Use this order:
  > 
  > Cache first
  > ↓
  > Rules/simple logic
  > ↓
  > Small Ollama model
  > ↓
  > Large Ollama model
  > ↓
  > Cloud model
  > ↓
  > Human review
  > 
  > Never send full cOllama-Based Agent Monitoring Setup
  > 
  > Use Ollama local models to monitor the full SDLC pipeline.
  > 
  > 1. Core Monitoring Agents
  > Agent	What It Monitors
  > Prompt Monitor Agent	user prompt, missing context, unclear request
  > Prompt Safety Agent	PII, secrets, unsafe instruction, prompt injection
  > Planner Agent	task breakdown, workflow sequence
  > Code Review Agent	code quality, bugs, standards
  > Test Case Agent	missing test cases
  > Unit Test Agent	unit test generation and result
  > Integration Test Agent	API/service test result
  > Error Detection Agent	exceptions, failed jobs, stack traces
  > Log Analyzer Agent	application logs, API logs, model logs
  > Trace Analyzer Agent	trace_id, latency, bottleneck
  > Pipeline Monitor Agent	CI/CD status, build, deploy, rollback
  > Missing Feature Agent	gap between requirement and implementation
  > Feedback Agent	user feedback, reviewer comments
  > Regression Agent	old feature broken or not
  > Security Agent	access, secret leak, dependency risk
  > Performance Agent	latency, memory, CPU/GPU usage
  > Cost Agent	token count, model usage, infra cost
  > Documentation Agent	missing README, API docs, runbook
  > Recovery Agent	retry, checkpoint, resume after crash
  > Supervisor Agent	controls all agents and escalation
  > 2. Ollama Model Mapping
  > Task	Suggested Ollama Model
  > Prompt review	llama3.1, mistral, gemma2
  > Code review	codellama, deepseek-coder, qwen2.5-coder
  > Testing	qwen2.5-coder, codellama
  > Log analysis	llama3.1, mistral
  > Security review	llama3.1, mistral
  > Documentation	llama3.1, gemma2
  > Planning	llama3.1, mistral
  > 3. UI Dashboard Sections
  > UI Tab	Shows
  > Prompt Input	all prompts by user, department, time
  > Plan	generated plan and task status
  > Code	files changed, review comments
  > Testing	test cases, pass/fail, coverage
  > Errors	failed step, stack trace, fix suggestion
  > Logs	searchable logs by trace_id
  > Tracing	UI → API → agent → tool → DB
  > Pipeline	build, test, deploy, rollback
  > Missing Features	requirement gaps
  > Feedback	user/reviewer feedback
  > Agent Health	agent success/failure
  > Model Health	Ollama model status, latency
  > Recovery	retry, checkpoint, resume
  > 4. Flow
  > User Prompt
  >   ↓
  > Prompt Monitor Agent
  >   ↓
  > Planner Agent
  >   ↓
  > Code / RAG / Tool Agents
  >   ↓
  > Code Review Agent
  >   ↓
  > Testing Agent
  >   ↓
  > Error + Log + Trace Agents
  >   ↓
  > Security Agent
  >   ↓
  > Reviewer Agent
  >   ↓
  > Feedback Agent
  >   ↓
  > Supervisor Agent Decision
  >   ↓
  > Final Output / Human Approval
  > 5. Database Tables
  > Table	Purpose
  > prompt_log	all input prompts
  > agent_run	each agent execution
  > model_run	Ollama model call
  > code_review_log	code issues
  > test_result	test cases and result
  > error_log	exceptions and failures
  > trace_log	request trace
  > pipeline_run	CI/CD status
  > feature_gap	missing feature list
  > feedback_log	user/reviewer feedback
  > checkpoint_store	resume after crash
  > 6. Terminal Example
  > [REQUEST] id=req-1001 user=praveen department=AI
  > [PROMPT_MONITOR] status=passed missing_context=false
  > [PLANNER] tasks=6 model=llama3.1
  > [CODE_REVIEW] issues=3 model=qwen2.5-coder
  > [TEST_AGENT] total=24 passed=21 failed=3
  > [ERROR_AGENT] error_found=true severity=medium
  > [TRACE] bottleneck=retrieval_service latency=2200ms
  > [PIPELINE] build=passed deploy=waiting_approval
  > [FEEDBACK] reviewer_status=pending
  > [SUPERVISOR] decision=send_to_human_review
  > 7. Brutal Rule
  > 
  > For Ollama local agent system, you must track:
  > 
  > prompt → plan → code → test → error → log → trace → pipeline → review → feedback → checkpoint
  > 
  > Otherwise you cannot debug, recover, or prove quality.Global Policy to Prevent These Issues
  > 1. Global Naming Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > No hardcoded project names	use {PROJECT_CODE}
  > No hardcoded folder paths	use config/env variable
  > No old labels	UI labels come from database
  > No manual rename only	use rename script + validation
  > Unique namespace	tenant.project.env.service
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > acme.claims.dev.rag-service
  > acme.claims.prod.agent-orchestrator
  > 2. Global Configuration Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > All URLs in config	no URL inside code
  > All secrets in vault	never in .env for production
  > Separate config per env	dev, test, stage, prod
  > Config validation required	app cannot start if config missing
  > Config versioning	every release stores config version
  > 3. Global Copy / Clone Project Policy
  > 
  > Before copying project:
  > 
  > Step	Required Action
  > 1	create new project_id and tenant_id
  > 2	generate new folder namespace
  > 3	create new database schema
  > 4	create new vector index
  > 5	create new prompt set
  > 6	create new MCP/tool config
  > 7	run global rename scanner
  > 8	run security validation
  > 9	run benchmark test
  > 10	get approval before production
  > 4. Global Agent Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Every agent has owner	business owner + tech owner
  > Every agent has permission	read/write/tool/action limits
  > Every agent has version	agent version locked per release
  > No agent unlimited access	least privilege only
  > Supervisor mandatory	no direct uncontrolled execution
  > Human approval required	for risky actions
  > 5. Global MCP / Tool Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Tool registry required	no hidden tools
  > Schema version required	input/output contract version
  > Auth required	no unauthenticated tool
  > Tool timeout required	every tool has timeout
  > Tool audit required	log every call
  > Dangerous tool restricted	delete/send/update needs approval
  > 6. Global RAG Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > New project = new index	never reuse old vector index blindly
  > Metadata mandatory	tenant, department, source, ACL
  > Citation mandatory	answer must link to source
  > ACL filtering mandatory	before retrieval and after retrieval
  > Index version required	track document and embedding version
  > Reindex required	after major data/schema change
  > 7. Global Text2SQL Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Semantic layer required	model cannot guess raw schema
  > SQL validation required	before execution
  > Read-only by default	no write/delete SQL unless approved
  > Row-level security	enforce tenant/user permissions
  > Query explanation	show table, join, filter logic
  > Limit required	avoid full table scan
  > 8. Global Fine-Tuning Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Dataset approval required	before training
  > PII scan required	before training
  > Eval set required	train/validation/test split
  > Model registry required	base model, data version, score
  > Rollback required	previous model available
  > Drift monitoring required	compare performance over time
  > 9. Global API Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > API versioning	/v1, /v2
  > Contract testing	frontend/backend schema check
  > Correlation ID	every request
  > Rate limit	per user/team/tenant
  > Timeout/retry	standard policy
  > Idempotency key	for write operations
  > Error standard	common error format
  > 10. Global UI Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > UI labels from config/database	not hardcoded
  > Prompt history visible	by department/user/date
  > Agent trace visible	for admin/support
  > Approval queue visible	pending/rejected/approved
  > Error view visible	user-friendly + technical details
  > Version visible	prompt/model/index/workflow version
  > Export available	audit CSV/PDF
  > 11. Global Accuracy / Benchmark Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Baseline required	before AI release
  > Golden dataset required	per department/use case
  > Regression required	before deployment
  > Accuracy threshold	defined by business
  > Human review score	required for high-risk output
  > Cost/latency benchmark	required before scale
  > Release gate	cannot deploy if score drops
  > 12. Global Data Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Data owner required	each source has owner
  > Data classification	public/internal/confidential/PII
  > Metadata mandatory	source, date, department, ACL
  > Lineage required	source → chunk → embedding → answer
  > Retention policy	delete/archive rules
  > Quality check	duplicate, missing, stale data
  > Schema drift alert	detect table/column change
  > 13. Global Model Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Model registry required	provider, version, cost, context
  > Model selection documented	selected/rejected reason
  > Fallback model required	primary + secondary
  > Token budget required	per request/user/team
  > Prompt version locked	no silent change
  > Output validation required	before final answer
  > Model monitoring	quality, latency, cost, drift
  > 14. Global Observability Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > Trace ID required	UI → API → agent → MCP → DB
  > Central logging	ELK/Grafana/Datadog
  > Metrics required	latency, cost, error, quality
  > Alerting required	failure, cost spike, SLA breach
  > Dashboard required	business + technical view
  > Incident record	RCA, owner, fix, prevention
  > 15. Global Recovery Policy
  > Rule	Standard
  > State machine required	every workflow status tracked
  > Checkpoint required	after every major step
  > Resume required	after crash/restart
  > Dead letter queue	failed tasks stored
  > Retry limit	avoid infinite loop
  > Rollback required	prompt/model/workflow rollback
  > Kill switch required	disable bad agent/tool
  > Final Global Rule
  > 
  > Every project must be:
  > 
  > config-driven
  > registry-driven
  > version-controlled
  > permission-controlled
  > traceable
  > testable
  > recoverable
  > auditable
  > rollback-ready
  > Production Gate
  > 
  > Do not move to production unless these are passed:
  > 
  > Naming check
  > Config check
  > Security check
  > RAG index check
  > Prompt check
  > Agent permission check
  > API contract check
  > UI label check
  > Benchmark check
  > Recovery check
  > Audit check
  > Rollback checkI’ll group the issues by layer so you can use it as a production risk checklist when copying or scaling one project into another.
  > 
  > Multi-Agent + MCP + RAG + Text2SQL + Fine-Tune — Issue List
  > 1. Project Copy / Global Rename Issues
  > Issue	Example
  > Hardcoded project name	old project name inside code/config
  > Shared folder path broken	/projectA/rag/index still used
  > Global variable mismatch	BANK_AGENT_NAME used in healthcare project
  > Environment file not updated	.env, secrets, API URLs
  > Namespace conflict	same agent_id across projects
  > Old database schema used	project copied but DB still points to old tables
  > Wrong vector index	new project reads old embeddings
  > Prompt still old domain	banking prompt used for insurance
  > Old tenant ID	data leakage risk
  > Old API endpoint	calls previous project service
  > 2. Multi-Agent Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Agent loop	cost and latency spike
  > Wrong agent routing	bad answer/output
  > Supervisor failure	full workflow stuck
  > No state tracking	cannot resume after crash
  > Agent role overlap	duplicate work
  > Conflicting agent outputs	reviewer cannot decide
  > Missing escalation	human not involved when needed
  > No permission control	agent accesses wrong data
  > No retry logic	simple failure breaks flow
  > No idempotency	duplicate email/API/action
  > 3. MCP Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > MCP server down	tool call fails
  > Tool schema mismatch	bad input/output
  > Version mismatch	old tool contract breaks agent
  > Missing auth	API rejected
  > Token expired	intermittent failure
  > Too many tools exposed	wrong tool selected
  > Tool timeout	workflow stuck
  > No tool audit	cannot prove what happened
  > Unsafe tool permission	agent can delete/send/update
  > No fallback tool	manual recovery needed
  > 4. Hyperscaler Issues
  > 
  > AWS / Azure / GCP
  > 
  > Issue	Impact
  > Wrong region	latency/compliance issue
  > IAM/RBAC mismatch	access denied
  > Secret not copied	service fails
  > Quota limit	model/API unavailable
  > Cost spike	uncontrolled usage
  > Network/VPC issue	service cannot connect
  > Storage permission	files not readable
  > Logging disabled	no debugging
  > Different service names	deployment failure
  > Vendor lock-in	hard migration
  > 5. RAG Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Bad chunking	poor retrieval
  > Wrong embedding model	low similarity
  > Old vector index	stale answers
  > Missing metadata	no filtering by dept/user
  > No document ACL	data leakage
  > Low top-k recall	missing context
  > Too much context	model confusion
  > Bad reranker	wrong document selected
  > No citation	user cannot trust answer
  > Hallucination	unsupported answer
  > 6. Text2SQL Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Wrong schema mapping	wrong SQL
  > Table name changed	query fails
  > Column name changed	query fails
  > No semantic layer	model guesses
  > Join confusion	wrong result
  > Aggregation mistake	wrong KPI
  > Date filter error	wrong reporting period
  > Unsafe SQL	data/security risk
  > No SQL validation	bad query executed
  > No row-level security	unauthorized data shown
  > 7. Fine-Tuning Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Bad training data	poor model
  > Data leakage	sensitive info learned
  > Overfitting	works only on examples
  > No eval set	cannot measure quality
  > Wrong base model	weak performance
  > Prompt format mismatch	bad inference
  > Version not tracked	cannot reproduce
  > No rollback	bad model stuck in prod
  > Drift	quality drops over time
  > High cost	training not worth it
  > 8. API Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Contract mismatch	frontend/backend break
  > No versioning	old clients fail
  > Timeout missing	hanging request
  > Rate limit missing	system overload
  > Bad error message	hard troubleshooting
  > No correlation ID	no trace
  > Auth bug	security risk
  > Payload too large	failure
  > Retry creates duplicate	duplicate action
  > No API gateway policy	weak control
  > 9. Frontend / UI Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > No workflow status	user confused
  > No agent trace	cannot debug
  > No prompt history	cannot audit
  > No approval screen	risky automation
  > No error detail	support blocked
  > No department filter	hard to manage
  > No version view	old/new confusion
  > No citation display	low trust
  > No retry button	manual DB fix needed
  > No admin control	cannot disable broken agent
  > 10. Accuracy / Benchmarking Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > No baseline	cannot prove improvement
  > No golden dataset	no standard test
  > Accuracy unclear	business does not trust
  > Only manual testing	slow and subjective
  > No regression test	old use case breaks
  > No RAGAS/DeepEval	weak evaluation
  > No human review score	quality gap
  > No benchmark by department	generic score misleading
  > No latency benchmark	performance unknown
  > No cost benchmark	ROI unclear
  > 11. Data Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Poor data quality	bad answers
  > Duplicate files	conflicting output
  > Missing metadata	weak filtering
  > Old data	stale answer
  > Unstructured format	parsing failure
  > PII present	compliance risk
  > No lineage	cannot trace answer
  > Schema drift	pipeline breaks
  > Access mismatch	data leakage
  > No data owner	no accountability
  > 12. Model Issues
  > Issue	Impact
  > Wrong model selected	poor quality/cost
  > Context limit hit	missing data
  > Model hallucination	false answer
  > Model unavailable	outage
  > Latency high	bad UX
  > Token cost high	budget issue
  > No fallback	workflow fails
  > Prompt sensitivity	unstable output
  > Model drift	output changes
  > No version lock	cannot reproduce
  > Final Brutal Checklist
  > 
  > Before copying one project to another, check:
  > 
  > Check	Must Verify
  > Project name	changed everywhere
  > Folder path	no old project path
  > Environment	.env, secrets, URLs
  > Database	schema, tables, tenant_id
  > Vector DB	new index/collection
  > Prompts	new domain wording
  > Agents	names, roles, permissions
  > MCP tools	endpoint, auth, schema
  > APIs	base URL, version
  > UI labels	department, workflow, project
  > Benchmarks	new golden test set
  > Security	RBAC, ACL, PII
  > Logs	trace_id, request_id
  > Deployment	namespace, region, config
  > 
  > Brutal truth: most copied AI projects fail because old names, old prompts, old indexes, old secrets, and old permissions are still hidden inside the new project.

## 2026-06-11T00:08:47.484062+00:00 · 27c48058
- **Source**: claude_code
- **Category**: user
- **Session**: 2026-06-10
- **Prompt**:

  > You are now entering the UI/Frontend Governance Policy, which is often forgotten in AI projects.
  > 
  > Most AI teams focus on agents, RAG, models, and APIs, but many production issues come from the UI layer.
  > 
  > Frontend Global Policy
  > 1. UI State Management Policy
  > Issue	Policy
  > Refresh loses data	Auto-save state
  > Browser refresh resets workflow	Recover from DB/session
  > User closes browser	Resume workflow later
  > Agent still running	Show live status
  > Multiple tabs	State synchronization
  > Session timeout	Save checkpoint
  > Browser crash	Resume from last state
  > 
  > Store:
  > 
  > User State
  > Workflow State
  > Agent State
  > UI State
  > Filter State
  > Tab State
  > Form State
  > 2. F12 / Browser Developer Tools Issues
  > Common Problems
  > Problem	Risk
  > API URL exposed	Security concern
  > Internal IDs exposed	Information leakage
  > JWT visible	Token theft
  > Sensitive data in console	PII exposure
  > Debug mode enabled	Security issue
  > Stack traces exposed	Attack surface
  > Hidden UI actions visible	Unauthorized access
  > 
  > Policy:
  > 
  > No secrets in browser
  > No connection strings
  > No API keys
  > No internal passwords
  > No debug logs in production
  > 3. UI Refresh Policy
  > User Refreshes Browser
  > F5
  > CTRL+R
  > Browser Restart
  > Machine Restart
  > 
  > Must recover:
  > 
  > Recover Item	Required
  > Current workflow	Yes
  > Current prompt	Yes
  > Uploaded files	Yes
  > Current status	Yes
  > Agent progress	Yes
  > Filters	Yes
  > Open tabs	Optional
  > Last output	Yes
  > 4. Background Processing Policy
  > 
  > UI should never depend on browser being open.
  > 
  > Bad:
  > 
  > Browser Open
  > ↓
  > Workflow Running
  > ↓
  > Browser Closed
  > ↓
  > Workflow Stops
  > 
  > Good:
  > 
  > Browser Open
  > ↓
  > Workflow Submitted
  > ↓
  > Backend Queue
  > ↓
  > Workflow Continues
  > ↓
  > User Returns Later
  > ↓
  > Status Loaded
  > 5. Frontend Error Handling Policy
  > Error Type	Required
  > API Failure	Show retry
  > Timeout	Show progress
  > Validation Error	Show field
  > Agent Failure	Show workflow status
  > File Upload Error	Resume upload
  > Network Error	Auto reconnect
  > Session Expired	Re-login
  > Permission Error	Clear explanation
  > 6. UI Color Policy
  > White Background Problems
  > Problem	Solution
  > White flash on refresh	Skeleton loading
  > Empty white screen	Error boundary
  > Loading confusion	Spinner/progress
  > Agent running but blank	Status banner
  > Failed API returns white page	Error page
  > 
  > Never show:
  > 
  > Blank White Screen
  > 
  > Always show:
  > 
  > Loading...
  > Recovering...
  > Retrying...
  > Workflow Running...
  > 7. Frontend Monitoring Policy
  > 
  > Track:
  > 
  > Metric	Purpose
  > Page Load	Performance
  > API Time	Backend issue
  > Component Error	UI bug
  > User Clicks	Adoption
  > Failed Requests	Stability
  > Refresh Count	UX problem
  > Browser Type	Compatibility
  > Device Type	Support
  > Screen Resolution	UI issue
  > 8. API + UI Synchronization
  > 
  > Problem:
  > 
  > Backend = Completed
  > Frontend = Running
  > 
  > Solution:
  > 
  > WebSocket
  > SignalR
  > SSE
  > Polling
  > 
  > Status Sync Required:
  > 
  > Status	UI
  > Created	Show
  > Running	Show
  > Failed	Show
  > Retrying	Show
  > Waiting Approval	Show
  > Completed	Show
  > 9. Frontend Testing Policy
  > Test	Required
  > Unit Testing	Yes
  > Component Testing	Yes
  > Integration Testing	Yes
  > E2E Testing	Yes
  > Browser Testing	Yes
  > Mobile Testing	Yes
  > Accessibility Testing	Yes
  > Performance Testing	Yes
  > Security Testing	Yes
  > 
  > Tools:
  > 
  > Playwright
  > Cypress
  > Selenium
  > 10. UI Status Banner Policy
  > 
  > Always visible:
  > 
  > Workflow ID
  > Status
  > Current Agent
  > Current Step
  > Progress %
  > Last Updated
  > Trace ID
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Workflow: WF-1001
  > Status: Running
  > Current Agent: Reviewer Agent
  > Progress: 78%
  > Last Updated: 14:25
  > Trace: TRC-9901
  > 11. Frontend Audit Policy
  > 
  > Store:
  > 
  > Event	Track
  > Login	Yes
  > Logout	Yes
  > Refresh	Yes
  > Prompt Submit	Yes
  > File Upload	Yes
  > Approval	Yes
  > Reject	Yes
  > Export	Yes
  > Download	Yes
  > Error	Yes
  > 12. Most Forgotten Frontend Issues
  > Issue	Happens Often
  > Browser refresh loses workflow	Very common
  > User opens 2 tabs	Very common
  > Stale cache	Very common
  > Old JS bundle	Common
  > Wrong state after retry	Common
  > File upload interrupted	Common
  > WebSocket disconnected	Common
  > Large table freeze	Common
  > Infinite spinner	Common
  > White screen of death	Common
  > Memory leak in browser	Common
  > Session timeout	Common
  > Slow rendering	Common
  > Duplicate submit button	Common
  > User double clicks	Common
  > Enterprise Rule
  > 
  > For every AI workflow:
  > 
  > Frontend State
  > +
  > Backend State
  > +
  > Workflow State
  > +
  > Agent State
  > +
  > Database State
  > +
  > Cache State
  > 
  > must always be synchronized.
  > 
  > If one state becomes inconsistent, users will see incorrect status, lost work, duplicate requests, or blank screens.

## 2026-06-11T01:24:34.963113+00:00 · f66853b4
- **Source**: claude_code
- **Category**: user
- **Session**: 2026-06-10
- **Prompt**:

  > For a production AI platform, most teams build only Generative AI and forget the other AI layers.
  > 
  > A complete enterprise AI workflow should have multiple AI types working together.
  > 
  > AI Processing Layers
  > Input
  >  ↓
  > Descriptive AI
  >  ↓
  > Diagnostic AI
  >  ↓
  > Predictive AI
  >  ↓
  > Prescriptive AI
  >  ↓
  > Generative AI
  >  ↓
  > Validation AI
  >  ↓
  > Verification AI
  >  ↓
  > Comparison AI
  >  ↓
  > Reflection AI
  >  ↓
  > Improvement / Inflection AI
  >  ↓
  > Human Review
  >  ↓
  > Output
  > 1. Descriptive AI
  > Question
  > What happened?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Summarize current and historical data.
  > 
  > Examples
  > Domain	Example
  > Banking	Monthly transactions
  > Insurance	Claims summary
  > HR	Employee turnover
  > Sales	Revenue dashboard
  > Operations	Incident report
  > Output
  > Facts
  > Metrics
  > Trends
  > Statistics
  > 2. Diagnostic AI
  > Question
  > Why did it happen?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Root cause analysis.
  > 
  > Examples
  > Problem	Diagnosis
  > Revenue drop	Customer churn
  > SLA failure	API latency
  > Low accuracy	Poor chunking
  > Fraud increase	New attack pattern
  > 3. Predictive AI
  > Question
  > What will happen?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Forecast future outcomes.
  > 
  > Examples
  > Area	Prediction
  > Sales	Future revenue
  > Banking	Loan default
  > Insurance	Claim probability
  > Healthcare	Readmission risk
  > 4. Prescriptive AI
  > Question
  > What should we do?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Recommend actions.
  > 
  > Example
  > Customer likely to churn.
  > Offer retention discount.
  > 5. Generative AI
  > Question
  > Create something.
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Generate:
  > 
  > Documents
  > Code
  > Reports
  > Emails
  > Summaries
  > SQL
  > Architecture
  > 6. Validation AI
  > Question
  > Is this valid?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Check:
  > 
  > Validation Type	Example
  > Business	Rule validation
  > Data	Schema validation
  > Security	Policy validation
  > API	Request validation
  > Architecture	Pattern validation
  > 7. Verification AI
  > Question
  > Is it true?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Verify claims.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Generated answer
  > ↓
  > Check source documents
  > ↓
  > Verify citation
  > ↓
  > Verify accuracy
  > 8. Comparison AI
  > Question
  > Which option is better?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Compare:
  > 
  > Compare	Example
  > Model	GPT vs Claude
  > Agent	Agent A vs Agent B
  > Architecture	Monolith vs Microservice
  > Prompt	Prompt V1 vs V2
  > Code	Old vs New
  > 9. Reflection AI
  > Question
  > Did I make a mistake?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Self-review.
  > 
  > Example:
  > 
  > Generate answer
  > ↓
  > Review answer
  > ↓
  > Identify weaknesses
  > ↓
  > Improve answer
  > 10. Inflection / Improvement AI
  > Question
  > How can I improve?
  > Purpose
  > 
  > Continuous optimization.
  > 
  > Checks:
  > 
  > Area	Example
  > Prompt	Better prompt
  > Agent	Better routing
  > Retrieval	Better chunking
  > Cost	Reduce tokens
  > Accuracy	Better model
  > 11. Validation AI Layers
  > 
  > A mature system validates everything.
  > 
  > Prompt Validation
  > Prompt complete?
  > Prompt ambiguous?
  > Prompt risky?
  > Prompt duplicate?
  > Data Validation
  > Missing values?
  > Schema mismatch?
  > Duplicate records?
  > Stale data?
  > Output Validation
  > Factually correct?
  > Cited?
  > Safe?
  > Complete?
  > Architecture Validation
  > Scalable?
  > Secure?
  > Recoverable?
  > Observable?
  > 12. Verification Pipeline
  > User Prompt
  >  ↓
  > Generate
  >  ↓
  > Validate
  >  ↓
  > Verify
  >  ↓
  > Compare
  >  ↓
  > Reflect
  >  ↓
  > Improve
  >  ↓
  > Approve
  >  ↓
  > Release
  > 13. AI Agents for Each Layer
  > Agent	Purpose
  > Descriptive Agent	Summarization
  > Diagnostic Agent	Root Cause
  > Predictive Agent	Forecast
  > Prescriptive Agent	Recommendation
  > Generative Agent	Create Content
  > Validation Agent	Check Rules
  > Verification Agent	Check Truth
  > Comparison Agent	Compare Results
  > Reflection Agent	Self Review
  > Improvement Agent	Optimization
  > Approval Agent	Human Approval
  > Audit Agent	Compliance
  > Enterprise AI Flow
  > Input AI
  >  ↓
  > Descriptive AI
  >  ↓
  > Diagnostic AI
  >  ↓
  > Predictive AI
  >  ↓
  > Prescriptive AI
  >  ↓
  > Generative AI
  >  ↓
  > Validation AI
  >  ↓
  > Verification AI
  >  ↓
  > Comparison AI
  >  ↓
  > Reflection AI
  >  ↓
  > Improvement AI
  >  ↓
  > Human Approval
  >  ↓
  > Output
  >  ↓
  > Feedback
  >  ↓
  > Learning Loop
  > Missing Layer Most Companies Forget
  > 
  > The most overlooked layers are:
  > 
  > Validation AI
  > Verification AI
  > Comparison AI
  > Reflection AI
  > Improvement AI
  > 
  > These layers often determine whether an AI system is reliable in production rather than just impressive in demos.
  > For an enterprise Group Chatbot, don't think of it as a single chatbot. Think of it as a multi-user collaborative AI workspace with agents, approvals, knowledge sharing, tracking, and governance.
  > 
  > Group Chatbot Architecture
  > Users
  >  ↓
  > Group Workspace
  >  ↓
  > Chat Orchestrator
  >  ↓
  > AI Agents
  >  ↓
  > RAG / MCP / APIs
  >  ↓
  > Validation & Review
  >  ↓
  > Approval
  >  ↓
  > Output
  >  ↓
  > Audit & Knowledge Base
  > Types of Group Chatbots
  > Type	Example
  > Team Chatbot	Development Team
  > Department Chatbot	HR, Finance
  > Project Chatbot	Project-specific
  > Incident Chatbot	Production Support
  > Meeting Chatbot	Meeting assistant
  > Knowledge Chatbot	Enterprise search
  > Approval Chatbot	Governance workflow
  > Multi-Agent Chatbot	Agent collaboration
  > Executive Chatbot	Management dashboard
  > Cross-Department Chatbot	HR + Finance + IT
  > User Roles
  > Role	Permissions
  > Admin	Full control
  > Manager	Approve, review
  > Team Lead	Assign tasks
  > Member	Ask questions
  > Reviewer	Validate output
  > Auditor	Read-only
  > AI Agent	Execute tasks
  > Group Chat Database Tables
  > chat_group
  > Field
  > group_id
  > group_name
  > department
  > project
  > owner
  > created_date
  > group_members
  > Field
  > member_id
  > group_id
  > user_id
  > role
  > joined_date
  > chat_message
  > Field
  > message_id
  > group_id
  > user_id
  > message
  > timestamp
  > message_type
  > 
  > message_type:
  > 
  > User
  > AI
  > System
  > Approval
  > Notification
  > Error
  > chat_attachment
  > Field
  > file_id
  > group_id
  > uploaded_by
  > file_name
  > file_type
  > upload_time

  > #cost-monitoring
  > #dr-recovery
  > #architecture-decisions
  > 
  > These channels become the operational memory of the AI platform and help prevent knowledge loss when teams change.Enterprise AI Group Chatbot — Phase 2 (Task, Workflow, Approval, Execution Layer)
  > 
  > Most teams build chat.
  > 
  > Production systems need:
  > 
  > Chat

  > Task Management

  > Workflow Engine

  > Approval Engine

  > Agent Execution

  > Audit Trail
  > 1. Chat → Task Conversion
  > Problem
  > 
  > User writes:
  > 
  > Build RAG System
  > 
  > Chat ends.
  > 
  > Nothing happens.
  > 
  > Solution
  > 
  > AI automatically creates:
  > 
  > Item	Example
  > Project	SharePoint RAG
  > Epic	Document Search
  > Feature	Hybrid Retrieval
  > Story	Upload Documents
  > Task	Build Chunking Service
  > Subtask	Create API
  > Database

  > task_id
  > project_id
  > title
  > description
  > priority
  > status
  > owner
  > created_by
  > created_date

  >

  > 
  > This is the foundation before adding Phase 3: Portfolio Management, Resource Planning, Capacity Planning, Financial Tracking, Agent Workforce Management, and Enterprise AI Operating Model.Enterprise AI Group Chatbot — Phase 3
  > Portfolio, Resource, Cost, Capacity, Agent Workforce
  > 1. Portfolio Management
  > View	What to Track
  > Project Portfolio	all AI projects
  > Department Portfolio	HR, Finance, IT, Sales
  > Use Case Portfolio	RAG, Text2SQL, Copilot, Agentic AI
  > Risk Portfolio	high-risk / blocked / delayed
  > Value Portfolio	cost saved, revenue, time saved
  > Compliance Portfolio	audit-ready / pending / failed
  > 2. Resource Planning
  > Resource	Track
  > Business Owner	decision, approval
  > Product Owner	backlog, priority
  > Architect	design, standards
  > Developer	implementation
  > QA	testing
  > Security	review
  > DevOps	deployment
  > Data Engineer	pipeline/index
  > AI Engineer	prompt/model/agent
  > Support	incident handling
  > 3. Capacity Planning
  > Area	Monitor
  > People Capacity	available hours
  > Agent Capacity	agent workload
  > Model Capacity	token/request limit
  > API Capacity	rate limits
  > Infra Capacity	CPU, RAM, GPU
  > Vector DB Capacity	index size, query load
  > Queue Capacity	backlog, wait time
  > Support Capacity	incidents per owner
  > 4. Financial Tracking / FinOps
  > Cost Type	Track
  > LLM Cost	token by model/user/dept
  > Cloud Cost	compute, storage, network
  > Vector DB Cost	index + query
  > MCP/API Cost	external calls
  > Development Cost	effort hours
  > Support Cost	incident hours
  > Rework Cost	failed release, bug fix
  > Savings	manual hours saved
  > 5. Agent Workforce Management
  > 
  > Treat agents like digital workers.
  > 
  > Agent Metric	Meaning
  > Agent Utilization	how often used
  > Agent Success Rate	completed tasks
  > Agent Failure Rate	failed tasks
  > Agent Cost	token/tool/API cost
  > Agent Quality Score	review result
  > Agent Latency	response time
  > Agent Owner	business + tech owner
  > Agent Retirement	remove unused/bad agents
  > 6. Executive Dashboard
  > Metric	Example
  > Total AI Projects	42
  > Active Workflows	128
  > Completed Workflows	2,450
  > Failed Workflows	38
  > Pending Approvals	17
  > Cost This Month	$18,500
  > Estimated Savings	$240,000
  > High-Risk Projects	5
  > SLA Breaches	3
  > Model Drift Alerts	2
  > 7. Portfolio Status
  > Status	Meaning
  > IDEA	use case proposed
  > DISCOVERY	business analysis
  > APPROVED	funded/accepted
  > IN_DESIGN	architecture work
  > IN_BUILD	development
  > IN_TEST	QA/UAT
  > READY_FOR_RELEASE	release approval
  > PRODUCTION	live
  > ON_HOLD	paused
  > RETIRED	stopped
  > 8. Portfolio Flow
  > Idea
  >  ↓
  > Business Value Review
  >  ↓
  > Risk Classification
  >  ↓
  > Architecture Review
  >  ↓
  > Budget Approval
  >  ↓
  > Build
  >  ↓
  > Test
  >  ↓
  > Release
  >  ↓
  > Monitor
  >  ↓
  > Optimize / Retire
  > 9. Database Tables
  > Table	Purpose
  > portfolio_project	all projects/use cases
  > resource_plan	people/resources assigned
  > capacity_plan	workload and availability
  > cost_log	model/cloud/API cost
  > value_log	ROI and savings
  > agent_workforce	agent inventory and KPIs
  > project_risk	portfolio risks
  > project_status_history	status changes
  > budget_tracker	planned vs actual cost
  > 10. Brutal Rule
  > 
  > A group chatbot becomes enterprise-grade only when it tracks:
  > 
  > Project
  > People
  > Agents
  > Cost
  > Risk
  > Capacity
  > Approval
  > Release
  > Incident
  > Business Value
  > 
  > Without this, it is just a chat UI — not an AI operating platform.u're describing is an Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix where every role follows the same lifecycle:
  > 
  > Input
  >  ↓
  > AS-IS Analysis
  >  ↓
  > Review
  >  ↓
  > Threshold Check
  >  ↓
  > Boundary Check
  >  ↓
  > Do's & Don'ts
  >  ↓
  > Design Specification
  >  ↓
  > Template
  >  ↓
  > Flowchart
  >  ↓
  > TO-BE Design
  >  ↓
  > Automation AI
  >  ↓
  > Human Review
  >  ↓
  > Feedback
  >  ↓
  > Continuous Improvement
  > Enterprise AI Delivery Matrix
  > Phase	Manager	BA	BRD	Project Plan	Product	Admin	DevOps	Architect	Lead	Developer	Tester	Security	Production
  > Input	Business Request	Requirement	Business Need	Timeline	Vision	Environment	Infra Need	Architecture Need	Scope	Feature Need	Test Need	Security Need	Support Need
  > AS-IS	Process Review	Current Process	Existing Rules	Existing Plan	Current Product	Current Setup	Existing Pipeline	Existing Architecture	Gap Review	Existing Code	Existing Test	Existing Controls	Existing Operations
  > Review	Manager Approval	Requirement Review	BRD Review	Plan Review	Product Review	Platform Review	DevOps Review	Design Review	Technical Review	Code Review	Test Review	Security Review	Ops Review
  > Threshold	KPI > 99%	Requirement Completeness	Business Approval	Schedule Confidence	Product Readiness	Availability	SLA	NFR	Design Quality	Code Quality	Test Coverage	Security Score	Production Readiness
  > Boundary	Scope	Requirement	Business Rule	Timeline	Feature	Platform	Environment	Architecture	Technical	Development	Testing	Security	Operations
  > Do's	Follow Process	Validate Requirements	Business Alignment	Track Progress	Prioritize	Govern Platform	Automate	Standardize	Guide Team	Build	Validate	Protect	Monitor
  > Don'ts	Scope Creep	Ambiguity	Missing Signoff	Unrealistic Dates	Gold Plating	Manual Secrets	Manual Deploy	Overengineering	No Standards	Hardcoding	Happy Path Only	Open Access	No Monitoring
  > Design Spec	Approval Model	Functional Spec	BRD	Delivery Plan	Product Roadmap	Admin Guide	Deployment Guide	Architecture Spec	Technical Design	Solution Design	Test Strategy	Security Design	Runbook
  > Template	Status Template	BRD Template	Business Template	Plan Template	Product Template	Admin Template	DevOps Template	Architecture Template	Design Template	Coding Template	Test Template	Security Template	Support Template
  > Flowchart	Governance Flow	Requirement Flow	Business Flow	Delivery Flow	Product Flow	Admin Flow	CI/CD Flow	Architecture Flow	Development Flow	Coding Flow	Test Flow	Security Flow	Incident Flow
  > TO-BE	Future State	Future Process	Future Business	Future Delivery	Future Product	Future Platform	Future Pipeline	Future Architecture	Future Team Model	Future Codebase	Future QA	Future Security	Future Operations
  > Automation AI	Status AI	Requirement AI	BRD AI	Planning AI	Product AI	Admin AI	DevOps AI	Architect AI	Lead AI	Coding AI	Testing AI	Security AI	Ops AI
  > Human Review	Manager	BA	Business	PM	Product Owner	Admin	DevOps Lead	Architect	Tech Lead	Senior Dev	QA Lead	Security Lead	Operations Lead
  > Feedback	KPI Feedback	Requirement Feedback	Business Feedback	Delivery Feedback	Product Feedback	Platform Feedback	Pipeline Feedback	Architecture Feedback	Technical Feedback	Code Feedback	Test Feedback	Security Feedback	Incident Feedback
  > Improvement	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous	Continuous
  > AI Artifacts Generated in Each Phase
  > Artifact	AI Generates
  > Email	requirement summary, status update
  > Demo	PoC, prototype
  > Scope	project scope
  > AS-IS	current process documentation
  > Gap Analysis	AS-IS vs TO-BE
  > BRD	business requirements
  > User Stories	backlog
  > Architecture	HLD, LLD, C4
  > Flowchart	process flow
  > Sequence Diagram	interaction flow
  > Test Cases	QA artifacts
  > Security Checklist	compliance controls
  > Runbook	support guide
  > Status Report	executive reporting
  > Lessons Learned	knowledge repository
  > Mandatory Feedback Loops
  > 
  > Every phase should have 3 feedback cycles:
  > 
  > AI Output
  >  ↓
  > Human Review
  >  ↓
  > Feedback
  >  ↓
  > AI Correction
  >  ↓
  > Validation
  >  ↓
  > Approval
  > Feedback Type 1
  > 
  > Business Feedback
  > 
  > Feedback Type 2
  > 
  > Technical Feedback
  > 
  > Feedback Type 3
  > 
  > Production Feedback
  > 
  > Enterprise AI Governance Rule
  > 
  > Nothing moves to the next phase unless:
  > 
  > Review Complete
  > +
  > Threshold Met
  > +
  > Boundary Checked
  > +
  > Validation Passed
  > +
  > Human Approved
  > +
  > Feedback Applied
  > 
  > This creates a repeatable AI-driven SDLC process from presales → BRD → architecture → development → testing → security → production → support → continuous improvement.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 2
  > AI Review, Validation, Verification, Benchmarking, Approval Framework
  > 
  > Most organizations stop at:
  > 
  > Input
  > ↓
  > AI Output
  > ↓
  > Done
  > 
  > Production systems require:
  > 
  > Input
  > ↓
  > AI Output
  > ↓
  > Validation
  > ↓
  > Verification
  > ↓
  > Benchmark
  > ↓
  > Comparison
  > ↓
  > Review
  > ↓
  > Approval
  > ↓
  > Release
  > 1. Validation Layer
  > Purpose
  > Did AI follow the instructions?
  > Area	Validation
  > Requirement	Complete?
  > Architecture	Standards followed?
  > Code	Compiles?
  > API	Contract valid?
  > Testing	Coverage sufficient?
  > Security	Policies followed?
  > Production	Deployment checklist complete?
  > Validation Agent
  > Input	Output
  > AI Artifact	Pass/Fail
  > Document	Validation Report
  > Code	Code Quality Score
  > Design	Architecture Score
  > 2. Verification Layer
  > Purpose
  > Is the content correct?
  > Area	Verification
  > Requirement	Business confirms
  > Architecture	Architect confirms
  > Code	Developer confirms
  > Testing	QA confirms
  > Security	Security confirms
  > Production	Ops confirms
  > Verification Output
  > Verified
  > Partially Verified
  > Rejected
  > Needs Review
  > 3. Comparison Layer
  > 
  > AI compares:
  > 
  > Compare	Example
  > AS-IS vs TO-BE	Process
  > Design A vs B	Architecture
  > GPT vs Claude	Model
  > Agent A vs B	Agent
  > Prompt V1 vs V2	Prompt
  > Release 1 vs 2	Deployment
  > Comparison Scorecard
  > Metric
  > Accuracy
  > Cost
  > Complexity
  > Scalability
  > Security
  > Maintainability
  > Risk
  > 4. Benchmark Layer
  > Benchmark Categories
  > Category	Example
  > Functional	Requirement Coverage
  > Performance	Response Time
  > Security	Vulnerability Count
  > Cost	Monthly Spend
  > Quality	Defect Leakage
  > RAG	Recall Precision
  > Agent	Success Rate
  > Benchmark Table
  > Area	Threshold
  > Accuracy	95%
  > Citation Accuracy	98%
  > Test Coverage	85%
  > Security Score	95%
  > Uptime	99.9%
  > Recovery	< 30 min
  > Cost Variance	< 10%
  > 5. Review Layer
  > Human Review Roles
  > Artifact	Reviewer
  > BRD	Business
  > Product Plan	Product Owner
  > Architecture	Architect
  > Code	Lead Developer
  > Test Plan	QA Lead
  > Security	Security Lead
  > Release	Production Manager
  > AI Review Layer
  > 
  > AI reviewers:
  > 
  > Reviewer Agent	Checks
  > Business Reviewer	Requirement quality
  > Architect Reviewer	Design quality
  > Code Reviewer	Code quality
  > Test Reviewer	Test quality
  > Security Reviewer	Security controls
  > Production Reviewer	Deployment readiness
  > 6. Approval Layer
  > Approval Gates
  > Gate 1
  > Business Approval
  > 
  > Gate 2
  > Architecture Approval
  > 
  > Gate 3
  > Development Approval
  > 
  > Gate 4
  > Testing Approval
  > 
  > Gate 5
  > Security Approval
  > 
  > Gate 6
  > Production Approval
  > approval_master
  > Field
  > approval_id
  > workflow_id
  > phase
  > approver
  > status
  > comments
  > timestamp
  > 7. AI Confidence Framework
  > 
  > Every AI artifact receives:
  > 
  > Metric	Score
  > Confidence	0-100
  > Completeness	0-100
  > Risk	Low/Med/High
  > Business Impact	Low/Med/High
  > Security Impact	Low/Med/High
  > Recommendation	Approve/Review/Reject
  > 8. Red Flag Detection Agent
  > 
  > Automatically detect:
  > 
  > Missing Requirements
  > Missing Architecture
  > Missing Test Cases
  > Missing Security Controls
  > Missing Rollback Plan
  > Missing Runbook
  > Missing Approval
  > Missing Monitoring
  > Missing DR Plan
  > Missing Cost Estimate
  > 9. Enterprise Review Workflow
  > Requirement AI
  >  ↓
  > Requirement Review
  >  ↓
  > Architecture AI
  >  ↓
  > Architecture Review
  >  ↓
  > Development AI
  >  ↓
  > Code Review
  >  ↓
  > Testing AI
  >  ↓
  > QA Review
  >  ↓
  > Security AI
  >  ↓
  > Security Review
  >  ↓
  > Production AI
  >  ↓
  > Production Approval
  >  ↓
  > Release
  > 10. Dashboard
  > Executive Dashboard
  > KPI
  > Approval Rate
  > Rejection Rate
  > AI Accuracy
  > Release Readiness
  > Risk Score
  > Compliance Score
  > Delivery Dashboard
  > KPI
  > Open Reviews
  > Pending Approvals
  > Failed Validations
  > Benchmark Failures
  > Security Findings
  > Production Readiness
  > Phase 2 Deliverables
  > 
  > Every artifact should have:
  > 
  > AI Generated
  > ↓
  > Validated
  > ↓
  > Verified
  > ↓
  > Benchmarked
  > ↓
  > Reviewed
  > ↓
  > Approved
  > ↓
  > Released
  > ↓
  > Monitored
  > 
  > Without these layers, AI can generate content quickly, but there is no assurance that the content is correct, complete, secure, or production-ready.
  > 
  > Next Phase (Phase 3) would be the Enterprise AI Control Tower: portfolio management, agent workforce management, cost governance, model governance, prompt governance, incident management, audit, compliance, and executive reporting.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 3
  > AI Control Tower (Command Center)
  > 
  > This is where most companies fail.
  > 
  > They have:
  > 
  > Agents
  > RAG
  > Models
  > MCP
  > Copilots
  > 
  > But nobody knows:
  > 
  > Who owns them?
  > Who approved them?
  > How much do they cost?
  > Which one failed?
  > Which one is unused?
  > Which one is risky?
  > AI Control Tower
  > Executive Dashboard
  >          ↓
  > Portfolio Dashboard
  >          ↓
  > Program Dashboard
  >          ↓
  > Project Dashboard
  >          ↓
  > Workflow Dashboard
  >          ↓

  > Phase 3 Outcome
  > 
  > You now have:
  > 
  > AI Governance
  > AI Portfolio

  > AI Knowledge Management
  > AI Operations
  > 
  > This transforms the platform from a collection of AI tools into an Enterprise AI Operating System (AIOS) that can manage hundreds of agents, models, MCP servers, workflows, departments, and projects under a single governance framework.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 4
  > Autonomous Enterprise AI Operating System (AIOS)
  > 
  > Phase 1 = SDLC
  > Phase 2 = Validation & Approval
  > Phase 3 = Control Tower
  > 
  > Phase 4 is where the platform becomes self-managing.
  > 
  > AIOS Architecture
  > Executive AI
  >       ↓
  > Portfolio AI
  >       ↓
  > Program AI
  >       ↓
  > Project AI
  >       ↓
  > Workflow AI
  >       ↓
  > Agent Workforce AI
  >       ↓
  > Model AI
  >       ↓
  > MCP AI
  >       ↓
  > Infrastructure AI
  >       ↓
  > Operations AI
  > 1. Executive AI
  > 
  > Acts as virtual CIO/CTO advisor.
  > 
  > Responsibilities
  > Function	Example
  > Portfolio Health	Which projects are failing
  > Cost Analysis	Where money is spent
  > Resource Analysis	Team bottlenecks
  > Risk Analysis	High-risk projects
  > Strategy Alignment	Business goals
  > Investment Recommendation	Fund or stop project
  > Executive Dashboard
  > KPI
  > ROI
  > Cost
  > Adoption
  > Risk
  > Compliance
  > Satisfaction
  > 2. Portfolio AI
  > 
  > Monitors all projects.
  > 
  > Detects
  > Duplicate Projects
  > Duplicate Agents
  > Duplicate MCPs
  > Duplicate Models
  > Unused Systems
  > Recommendations
  > Merge Projects
  > Retire Projects
  > Increase Budget
  > Reduce Budget
  > Add Resources
  > 3. Program AI
  > 
  > Coordinates multiple projects.
  > 
  > Example
  > RAG Project
  > Text2SQL Project
  > Agent Platform
  > 
  > Shared:
  > 
  > Infrastructure
  > Agents
  > Models
  > MCP Servers
  > Detects
  > Issue
  > Dependency conflicts
  > Resource conflicts
  > Timeline conflicts
  > Budget conflicts
  > 4. Project AI
  > 
  > Acts as virtual project manager.
  > 
  > Automatically
  > Task
  > Create plan
  > Create backlog
  > Create user stories
  > Create status reports
  > Identify risks
  > Escalate blockers
  > 5. Workflow AI
  > 
  > Monitors:
  > 
  > All Workflows
  > All Approvals
  > All Tasks
  > All Releases
  > Detects
  > Issue
  > Stuck workflow
  > Missing approval
  > Delayed task
  > Failed release
  > Missing review
  > 6. Agent Workforce AI
  > 
  > Treat agents as employees.
  > 
  > agent_employee
  > Field
  > agent_id
  > role
  > manager
  > department
  > workload
  > performance
  > Agent Metrics

  > Productivity

  > Cost

  > Agent Workforce Optimization
  > 
  > Automatically:
  > 
  > Retire Agent
  > Replace Agent
  > Merge Agents
  > Split Agents
  > 7. Model Governance AI
  > 
  > Continuously evaluates models.
  > 
  > Model Comparison
  > Compare
  > GPT
  > Claude
  > Gemini
  > Llama
  > Mistral
  > Phi

  > Drift

  > Quality Drop

  > Switch Model

  > Rollback Model
  > 8. MCP Governance AI

  > Monitors:
  > 
  > MCP

  > Jira
  > SAP
  > Salesforce
  > GitHub
  > ServiceNow

  > Version Changes

  > GPU

  > Scale Up
  > Scale Down

  > Use Ollama

  > At Level 10, AI is not just answering questions—it is helping govern, operate, optimize, secure, monitor, and continuously improve the entire enterprise ecosystem.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 5
  > Enterprise AI Control Framework (People + Process + Technology + AI)
  > 
  > Phase 4 created the AI Operating System.
  > 
  > Phase 5 creates the Enterprise Governance Layer that auditors, CIOs, CTOs, CROs, and regulators care about.
  > 
  > Enterprise AI Governance Pyramid
  > Board / Executive Committee

  > AI Governance Council

  > Project Governance

  > Agent Governance

  > This is typically the level expected for a large enterprise AI platform supporting hundreds of users, dozens of agents, multiple models, MCP integrations, and regulated business processes.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 6
  > Enterprise AI Reference Architecture Repository
  > 
  > Phase 5 gave Governance.
  > 
  > Phase 6 gives a Reusable Enterprise AI Blueprint Library.
  > 
  > The biggest problem in large organizations:
  > 
  > Project 1 builds everything again
  > Project 2 builds everything again
  > Project 3 builds everything again
  > 
  > Result:
  > 
  > Duplicate Agents
  > Duplicate Prompts
  > Duplicate MCPs
  > Duplicate APIs
  > Duplicate Architectures
  > Duplicate Costs
  > Enterprise Reuse Strategy
  > Reference Architecture
  >         ↓
  > Reference Agent
  >         ↓
  > Reference Workflow
  >         ↓
  > Reference Prompt
  >         ↓
  > Reference MCP
  >         ↓
  > Reference API
  >         ↓
  > Reference Dashboard

  > allowing teams to discover, reuse, govern, rate, approve, and deploy enterprise AI assets instead of rebuilding them repeatedly.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 7
  > Enterprise AI Marketplace & Digital Workforce Exchange
  > 
  > Phase 6 built the AI Factory.
  > 
  > Phase 7 builds the Enterprise AI Marketplace where teams discover, reuse, govern, purchase, approve, deploy, monitor, and retire AI assets.
  >

  > The next logical phase is not more automation—it is Enterprise Intelligence, where AI continuously models business operations, predicts outcomes, recommends investments, and supports strategic decision-making across the organization.Enterprise AI SDLC Governance Matrix — Phase 9
  > Enterprise Intelligence Layer (EIL)
  > 
  > Phase 8 created an Autonomous Enterprise.
  > 
  > Phase 9 creates an Intelligent Enterprise.
  > 
  > The difference:
  > 
  > Autonomous Enterprise
  > Can execute work
  > Intelligent Enterprise
  > Can think about the business
  > Can predict outcomes
  > Can recommend actions
  > Can simulate scenarios
  > Can optimize investments
